<Author>airhart
<Content>Great little retreat after a day of work! After a frustrating search in an expensive city for a hotel that met my daily allowance for work travel, I found this hotel at the last minute, perhaps a cancellation in a sea of $600/night prices (some sort of convention in town). It was small, friendly, clean, and the attention to detail was wonderful after such a long day... my room was playing satellite radio classical music (not elevator-style, either) when I walked in. Everything was spotless, the bathroom was great, and although the view was of nothing but a wall, I didn't care at night after a long day. Not good for a long stay - the rooms come with impractical but charming minifridges, and the 'closets' are clever cubbyholes - but for one night, a perfect retreat. Morning oatmeal and the paper was nice too... a decent bar, and a friendly staff. Definite recommendation.

<Author>Aussie_Charlotte
<Content>Good Location, small room, good price for Boston We drove to Boston so parking was a bit of a problem. You have to park in a parking station about a 10 minute walk away. The hotel is on a busy road so there was no available parking spaces in any block near the hotel, let alone in front of the hotel and you can't double park to drop off your suitcases because of the traffic. We dragged our suitcases all the way from the parking station. It would be challenging if you had young children or elderly travellersThe hotel itself is modern and the rooms are clean and modern, though quite small - there really isn't anywhere aside to put your suitcases - wherever you put them, you will have to step over them to move around the room. There was free internet and a free breakfast. The Location is great - Boylston St has several bars, restaurants, the subway to downtown and there's a street that has upscale boutiques and shops that is one block away. The price was under $300 which is good for Boston.

<Author>shaun1967
<Content>Great Location I took this hotel on a recommendation via the Tripadvisor forum. The stay was booked a few months ago, just before the credit crisis was in full blown mode, so at the time I thought my successful bartering of a $15 discount on a queen room was a coup. Maybe the way things are $149 a night might get you a bit more, I don't know. Anyway, by pre-crash standards its a good deal. Location is great, rooms are modern, clean, good spec, loads of TV channels. Rooms are small - even the queen rooms, but that's already well documentedThe breakfast and lounge for us are a bonus (I use the present tense as I'm writing this up during our stay). Two free to use high speed internet terminals (always available, never a queue) is something not always complimentary. The breakfast also saves you a few bucks on your holiday budget and for most people the breakfast would be fine. A previous reviewer described it as little more than hard bagels and bitter coffee, but that is unfair. There are muffins, fresh bananas, apples, oranges, doughnuts, tea, orange juice and cereal. The fruit and beverages are available free in the lounge 24 hours in fact, plus the daily papers. There are no egg/quarter of a pig options, so if that is what rings your bell then the breakfast will be no bonus to youTraffic noise is something that seems to divide opinion, and I can say that from our sixth floor front facing room you can in fact hear the sounds from the street, but they are by no means insufferable. I guess it depends on what you are already accustomed to. I do appreciate that some people will be used to deathly quiet nights and a small amount of noise can be very unsettling. But that's a city centre location for you, nothing to do with the hotelReception/front desk staff? Some say can't do enough, some say cold and frosty. Well ... I can see both sides. What they do is get you what you want and answer all your questions without any fuss, what they don't do is fawn all over you, so again, if this is important to you ...All in all because of the location and general specification in context of a very competitive rate, I'd certainly stay here again

<Content>Excellent value, good location My husband and I had a pleasant stay at the Charlesmark. <Author>QueenieC
<Content>Excellent Charlesmark We have just returned from a week's holiday in Boston and stayed at the Charlesmark throughout.Having read the reviews on here we requested a Queen room on the 6th floor. This was perfect for our needs, we overlooked the Boston Public Library and the marathon finishing line. There was no noticeable noise and we were certainly not disturbed by anything.The room was not massive but plenty big enough and very comfortable. Not a lot of hanging space for clothes but loads of shelving space so that was not a problem, the iron and ironing board were a nice touch too. The shower room was excellent and a high quality range of toiletries were provided each day. TV/audio facilities were brilliant, the DVD/VHS library was a bonus - after a day's walking and sightseeing there were a couple of evenings when we did not feel like going out so just relaxed and watched a film in our room.The staff were exceptionally friendly and helpful, the rooms were very clean, there was tea/coffee/fresh orange availabe free of charge in the lounge 24/7 and bottled water left in the room each morning. Breakfast was fine, staff were vigilant in keeping everything topped up. Bagels/doughnuts/muffins/jams/cream cheese/oats/fresh fruit/coffee/tea/orange juice all very fresh and plentiful.Free use of internet and printer was very useful especially when it came to printing boarding passes for return journey.Very best of all though was the perfect location, right in the middle of everything with the green line T station just over the road. We loved Boston and cannot speak highly enough of the Charlesmark. We could not fault it or its staff in any way and would highly recommend it to everyone. If there was anything at all I could have wished for it would be a safe in the room but reception would have been happy for us to use their safe had we requested it.Go, go, go! Enjoy!!

<Author>AoSPR
<Content>Charlesmark perfect for Boston Let's first dispense with the only neg: yes, the rooms are small. But this is a small building and the spaces were very cleverly distributed. It was not uncomfortable at all. Room size is sufficient to crash after walking the city and they are fairly new, well decorated, very clean and I didn't experience any noise problems.Now with the good: This was my first time in Boston. I made the reservations by e-mail for pre and post cruise stays. The e-mail reservation was handled swiftly, as was my re-confirmation request.Price/value - I really looked around and couldn't find anything better in such a central location. $206.00 is really a good deal for this little jewel of a place.Location - Excellent. If the location was any better, it would probably be ruined. We walked everywhere from the hotel. Steps from the Prudential mall, T-Station, Newbury street, and right next to some pretty good restaurants (make reservations early).Check in - We first arrived around 6:00 Pm on a Friday and the check in process was fast and painless. Nice young lady at the desk. On our second check in, we arrived too early, but another nice young lady took our bags and was very dilligent in informing us when our room was ready. Our bags were waiting for us in the room.Facilities - Nice bar just off the lobby. Great bartenders. Good people-watching outside deck. PC's and laser jet printer available for guests just off the bar. Again, building is small but the elevator is full size.Food - The hotel has an adequate and basic breakfast available for free. There's a Thai restaurant right next door. I didn't try it but the other guests seem to like it. They serve in the hotel as if it were a hotel restaurant, but it is not. There are many nearby eating places, from cheap and fast to very upscale. On busy nights, wait times can be from one to two hours so make reservations early. We tried the Legal Seafoods at the nearby Prudential - overrated. We settled for the Cheesecake Factory also at Prudential (we had enough seafood and gourmet cooking during our cruise). It's the best value as restaurants here are too expensive.Attractions - I cannot emphasize enough about the central location of this place. In two hours, we leisurely walked from the hotel, to the Gardens, Commons, Freedom Trail up to the Quincy Market. We took the T green line back (that sucked). On an evening, we walked around Newbury just behind the hotel. Did I say that the hotel is in the middle of everything?Plumbing problems and such - NONE. Everything worked just fine.Check out - Also painless. We left early for the airport and the gentleman manning the desk was nice enough to help us with our bags and even risked life and limb to step into the street with a whistle and a flashlight to hail a cab from the nearby Lennox hotel for us. Before we had a chance to thank him, he was already walking away. I say this because he did so very professionally, not hanging around expecting a tip or anything.

<Author>auntietat
<Content>Perfect place to stay in Boston! Stayed at the Charlesmark from 9/29 to 10/4, based on the great reviews on Tripadvisor.com. We stayed (2 people) in room 501, Queen room on the 5th floor facing the street. We brought earplugs due to some of the reviews below, but I never ended up needing them. Even with the construction going on at the Boston Public Library directly across the street, it was not that noisy. The room was small-ish (like a lot of European hotels), but was totally fine. We had plenty of room to put our clothes on the bookshelves, and store our luggage away in the cabinet. Bed was super comfortable, shower was good. The only small qualm I had was that the room needed more lights/lamps. Location of the hotel was GREAT, and the staff at the Charlesmark were all very nice and helpful, too. Breakfast was fine (fresh fruit, oatmeal, coffee, tea, bagels, muffins, donuts), and there are 2 computers in the lounge for guests to use. Housekeeping did a great job of straightening the room everyday, and provided complimentary bottled water in the room each day! I would definitely stay here again.

<Author>lanneNL
<Content>lovely boutique hotel Just stayed in the Charlesmark Hotel in Boston, and it was definitely worth it!Okay, if you are looking for a big room in a chain 13-in-a-dozen hotel room, the charlesmark is not your place to be. If you are however looking for a charming hotel in an excellent location in Boston, this is it!The rooms are indeed small, but everything is custommade for the room, and you have a good bed, tv, stereo with in bathroom speakers, reading chair, airco and great bathroom with lovely shower. Add 2 free bottles of water daily, a lively hotel bar downstairs (open to public), free wireless internet and 2 computers for use downstairs, and good service to that, and you sort of have the charlesmark!There is a complimentary brekafast every morning with bagels, doughnuts and muffins and fruit. The location is execllent: across the street from copley square including T-station, around the corner from newburey street, and amidst all great restaurants, bars and shops from backbay (and copley square and prudential centre).Only minor side: as said, small rooms, and there is an AC-unit outside the back which you do hear, however, I have to say that I never woke up because of it, I just heard it when I accidentally woke up by something else!After all, I would definitely recommend the Charlesmark!

<Author>coatgirl
<Content>Not much charm, but go for the value and location This is, all in all, a very good choice for the budget-conscious tourist. It is definitely value for money - what you get for the price is an excellent location to base your sightseeing from and comfortable, clean rooms. It seems some rooms are noisy, so my advice is to arrive on or slightly before the check-in time to make sure you're happy with the room they give you. I arrived about 30 mins early, and discovered that the room allocated was on the 1st floor and facing into a tiny yard which was blocked in on all sides by the walls of the surrounding buildings. This yard contained the air conditioning units, so being on the first floor meant very high constant noise levels from the aircon units. I asked to be re-located, and was given a room on the 4th floor which was much much better. To their credit, they swapped our room with no fuss at all. On the other hand, we did specifically ask for a quiet room when we made our booking, so.......The rooms are comfortable, clean, and small but not too cramped. The ones at the back are rather dark so not particularly inviting in the daytime. I think it's a bit of a misdescription to say the hotel is boutique because it certainly doesn't have the style or design of a boutique hotel. I am surprised by the previous comment that the breakfast is awesome. Maybe I am used to the breakfasts in European hotels, which usually include hot buffets with sausage, egg, bacon, tomatoes etc. The breakfast here consists of: doughnuts from Dunkin Donuts, bagels from Finagle A Bagel, muffins (didn't see where they were from), and a basket of apples, bananas  oranges. It's okay, but certainly not awesome. The hotel and the staff are efficient but without charm but, given the price, don't expect anything more. For my three-night stay, I'm pretty sure I made the right choice.

<Content>Great location wonderful hotel We stayed at the Charlesmark Sept 21 and 22, 2008 and it was a wonderful choice. It's location almost across from the T is very convenient. <Author>GMY68
<Content>My second stay here was not as good as my first: noise was awful There are many fabulous things about this hotel, which I will lay out below. I enjoyed my first stay, a year ago, but my recent stay was sadly clouded by two extremely noisy and sleepless nights.I was given a standard room at the back of the hotel. You might think that this would be a quiet option (i.e. away from the main, busy street) but it was a bit of a nightmare, for two reasons. First, there's a very noisy vent that blows loudly through the night. With ear plugs, one can just about handle this. But second, at 3.30am every night an extremely loud garbage truck comes by, very slowly, to pick up what sound like glass bottles from the bins behind the restaurants. Yikes. It was really painful being woken up both nights by this crazy, crashing noise (I was in town to give some lectures, and so having sleep interrupted was a real downer).So you should be aware of this problem. If you are a very heavy sleeper, maybe you'll be fine.As for the great things, there are many:*Terrific location*Stylish design*Very friendly and helpful staff*Free wireless, two computers with printer (so you can check-in online for flights and print your boarding pass)*Very clean and comfortable rooms, with lots of nice touches e.g. free bottled water*The bar is lively and really a great place to meet friends*It is decent value for money.

<Author>agrippina1705
<Content>Great hotel in a lively part of the city We stayed at the Charlesmark hotel with friends for 5 nights in late August and thoroughly enjoyed our time there.The hotel rooms are small (around 3m by 5m for the main room) but it didn't bother us - we have stayed in smaller rooms in the US, and a lot of thought had clearly gone into making the most of the space (tabletop ironing board in the cupboard, pull-out bedside table space). The bed seemed to be a little bit short, though. The building is very overlooked but the hotel has venetian blinds for privacy. The bathroom was shower only, but it was great. The room itself was very clean and a good size and the shower was very powerful and hot. Shampoo, shower gel, body lotion and mouthwash were provided. The TV allows free access to hundreds of channels and there was also a DVD player and stereo in the room. Local phone calls are free - but longer distance or international calls are not available through the hotel's phone system; you have to buy a phone card from the CVS or Walgreen's stores (about 1-2 mins from the hotel) and use this to dial out. There were two internet terminals in the hotel lounge which were free to use (and very seldom in use!).There was no safe in the room, and no minibar. However, there was an icebucket, and ice was available from a machine on the first floor. The bar in the hotel was great (very strong cocktails!) so there wasn't much call for a minibar in any case. Housekeeping left two free bottles of water in the room each day. The best thing about the Charlesmark is the location - right in the centre of town opposite the public library and 2 minutes from the Copley T stop. The next street up is Newbury Street, which is great for shopping and even better for finding somewhere good to eat and drink in the evening. It was also easy to get around Boston from the hotel - both on foot and using the T. The hotel breakfast is basic and self-service but good quality: lots of different bagels (with jam and cream cheese), oatmeal sachets, doughnuts, muffins and fruit, plus coffee, fruit juice and iced water. For something more substantial, the cafe in the Trident Bookstore on Newbury Street serves really delicious cooked breakfasts. The Charlesmark is perfect if you want somewhere modern and central, and are planning on spending most of your time exploring the city. I would definitely stay there again.

<Author>cantwait2getthere
<Content>Mostly good Here's the good:-Very convenient location close to the T -Nicely furnished room and nice decor throughout the hotel.-Even though the hotel doesn't offer any official laundry service, the front desk staff accommodated our laundry needs by getting housekeeping to put a load on for us while we were out touring the city (for a $10 fee).-The hotel accommodated my request to have a room on one of the two top floors so that there was less street noise.-The variety of television channels was HUGE.The bad:-The room is indeed very small, though this didn't bother me all that much because boutique hotels in Boston and New York tend to be small, so I expected it.-The breakfast offered downstairs was sad. Hard-as-a-rock bagels and some bitter coffee doesn't really constitute breakfast in my mind. -The view from the room consisted of a brick wall about four feet from the window.All in all, yes, I would stay there again considering it was very centrally located and very clean, and it was one of the only hotels I could find in downtown Boston for under $200 a night. However, next time I would factor in the cost of eating breakfast out each morning when comparing prices.

<Author>The_Sherriff
<Content>Needs a little freshening up I stayed at the Charlesmark as an alternative to the mega-convention hotels in Back Bay for a major conference. It was mostly a very pleasant experience - the staff are particularly friendly and helpful and the rooms clean and well-equipped. They are small, but Boston hotel rooms often are and I found this one more manageable than the poky little closet that I got at the Omni Parker House last time I was in the city. The complimentary continental breakfast was good value, particularly when faced with a challenging day of eating for the company. The rooms are remarkably quiet considering the location on Boylston, which is quite a party street. The air conditioning is also discreet and effective so I got some really good sleep, which was much needed to work from 08:30 until 22:00. However, all the awards are for the opening in 2006 and some investment is becoming due. Frankly, the towels were threadbare and I would not have been surprised to put my feet through the sheets. I also had some intricate cross-cultural negotiations to get a plug for the bathroom hand-basin (or a stopper for the bathroom sink, if you are reading this in US English).

<Author>Pert_UK
<Content>Half excellent / Half Poor = Average Stayed at the Charlesmark in May 2008 for 2 nights, and I had a mixed experience.I arrived early (my fault) and my room wasn't ready. The receptionist checked for any available rooms but said the only one she had was near the bar and I had asked for a quiet one - top marks for knowing my request and acting on it. She said she'd ring me when my room was ready and took my mobile phone number - great. Unfortunately she never did ring, so that was a shame and left me wandering around the city for longer than I needed to, but not a big deal and she did store my luggage.I returned later that afternoon and they'd already moved my bags from their store up to my room - fantastic service! The room was very nice, wonderfully clean  beautifully decorated, with great attention to detail. Not a massive room, but perfectly fine - don't listen to the people whining about tiny tiny rooms and poor decoration, unless you're planning on bringing more than a couple of suitcases when it might get crowded.However, despite being given a quiet room overlooking an outdoor void / shaft surrounded by brick walls, I was repeatedly woken all night by a huge fan at the bottom of this void that kept starting up, running for 10 minutes and then shutting down again. Every time it restarted (regularly, roughly every 30 minutes) there was a large bang before the loud whirring started. I could have slept through the whirring, but the bang woke me up every time all night. There are several other rooms overlooking this fan, so I can't see how anybody in any of them could have got much sleep either.I complained the next morning and got moved to another room, which was actually bigger and nicer than the first, but at the front of the hotel. This was a bit noisier than I would have liked (you overlook the main road) but at least it quietened down later at night, unlike the fan.So what to conclude? I really liked the style of the hotel, the food downstairs from the Thai restaurant was excellent, the rooms were great and it's very good value. I was slightly annoyed that I ordered a gin and tonic from the bar and it was completely flat - when I called the waitress over she immediately asked if it was flat...so why did she give it to me? She replaced it very politely, with a fractionally less flat GT, but it was still far from sparkling.So I'm giving the Charlesmark an average rating because I really wouldn't go back there because I couldn't be sure I'd get any sleep. It's a real shame, as someone has obviously put a lot of effort into making it a stylish place to stay and the location is pretty good.  
<Date>Jun 19, 2008

<Author>DeDeOregon
<Content>Better than the first time! I stayed at the Charlesmark for business purposes at the end of March. It was the second time I had stayed there and I was again pleased with my stay. Since my first stay the lobby area, bar, and lounge had been completed and I was impressed with these new areas. The hotel has a modern vibe, but no so much that it feels sterile or impersonal in any way.My colleagues stayed at some of the big chain hotels nearby and I have to say that I was thrilled with my decision to stay at the Charlesmark. Their hotels were more expensive, impersonal, and were the typical cookie-cutter places that were connected to the mall or the conference center. Rooms in the Charlesmark are modest in size, but certainly adequate. Plus, it's Boston--get out and enjoy the city! The hotel is incredibly convenient, close to the conference center, the T, shopping, and restaurants but still allows you to feel like you've gotten away a little.My only minor complaint is that there can be considerable street noise, depending on what room you have. It's all part of the city experience though so I really didn't mind very much.

<Author>TRP1966
<Content>Great, Hip Bargain Hotel With Personality! I have just returned from a four night stay at the Charlesmark due to a business conference in Boston. I had done a lot of cheking prior to making a reservation because it is a pretty expensive town in which to stay, and even the conference rates for other hotels were out of my limited budget. Then I discovered the Charlesmark, which is a true diamond in the rough. Sandwiched between a Ritz Camera store and a really cool Thai place, the hotel is small and lean. I had read some critiques of the rooms being somewhat small and dark, and they were accurate. I could live with the size, but despite the best efforts of the staff, they could not find me a lamp. But that was cool, because the Charlesmark staff is second to none in terms of the personality and customer service skills of the staff. Unfortunately, I can't remember all the names, but Nikki - who took my reservation, helped get me a sweet deal (for the area) on the room and never acted annoyed with my umpteen million calls with an equal amount of questions; Vanessa at the bar who makes a mean margarita and always had a welcoming, friendly smile, and Scott, the other guy who worked the desk, stand out in particular. There are others, but in general, I was very happy with the staff, as many of the other area hotels won't give you the time of day when you call to ask a question, or need some help, or just a friendly face when your hoisting a drink or two at the end of the day. And the location of this place is awaesome as well, as you can pretty much walk to all the cool spots, and cabs are all over the place if you're not up to it. The only real negative, aside from the aforementioned minor inconveniences mentioned above is that there is a large population of homeless folks in this area, and while safety was never really a concern, they constantly hit you up for change. It got a to a point where I was recognizing them and even got a few of their names. But I understand this is a problem with the city in general, so it's not a beef with the hotel itself. Would I stay there again? You bet! In fact, I'd still be there now were it not for the fact that I have an early flight and wanted to be cloer to Logan. Plus they were booked tonight when I tried to add a fifth one on when my travel plans changed. But even then, they put me on a list to let me know if anything opened up, and no doubt would have set me up, as right as I was leaving, there was a cancellation. Unfortunately, I was set to get closer to Logan so I passed it up. I wouldn't stay here (sorry guys) if this were a family trip due to the room size, but if you're a business traveller on the go, or a couple looking for a cool place to stay for a Boston getaway, the Charlesmark could be your home for a few days. They sure treat you like family. Cool places nearby - Bukawski's, Uno, lenox, Whiskeys, ust to name a few. Hope this helps and that the good folks over there read this stuff too. And this is not something I usually do. Definately check this place out! Cheers...TRP in 403...

<Author>EuroReisen
<Content>Great location, great price I spent three nights at the Charlesmark and agree with many of the previous reviewers: the location and price can't be beat.The main purpose of my trip to Boston was shopping, and the location of the Charlesmark in the Back Bay neighborhood, just a block off Newbury and close to Copley Place, was ideal. Additionally, the T stop just down the street made getting around the rest of the city very easy. The price was also at least $100 cheaper than anything else I was able to find in the neighborhood.Other reviewers have raved about the friendly and attentive staff, but unfortunately this was not my experience. I arrived a couple hours before the check-in time, and my room was not yet ready, which I was expecting. I think the guy manning the desk was the same another review described as indifferent, and I agree; he wasn't exactly rude, but he also wasn't very helpful. Anyway, when I came back later close to the official check-in time, my room was ready, and my bags had already been brought up. By then, someone new was at the desk to actually check me in, and she was much more pleasant but still did not give me any information about the room, hotel, etc. For example, had I not read here that breakfast was provided in the lobby, I never would have known, as she didn't tell me and nothing in the Guest Information in the room mentioned it (and it was served in the upper lobby, tucked away from the elevator and flow of traffic). I overheard another guest checking in later during my stay, and she got a full spiel about breakfast, internet, etc. Also, during my four-day stay, I could hardly get anyone at the desk to look up, much less say hello, during my various comings and goings.I had a room on the sixth floor, and the view out the big windows was actually quite nice. The room was quite small by American standards but perfect for my needs (and not unexpected after reading previous reviews here). The DirectTV and radio were nice, as was the complimentary water. Overall, though, the room I had could use some TLC. The carpet in the bedroom was loose along one wall, especially outside the bathroom door, and caused me to catch my toe a time or two. A light bulb was out in the bathroom (and was not replaced during my stay), and a dial on the wall that I assume was volume control for the sound system didn't work. The room had a cordless phone, but the battery in the handset needed replacement, meaning all calls had to be quick to avoid being cut off when the battery died. The hotel also had free wireless internet access, but the signal was so weak in my room that it was essentially useless. And oddly, the room had a folding chair (not sure why) in the closet/cupboard but no suitcase stand, which would have been much more convenient than the floor.Other small things would really make a big difference: replace the thin blanket and bedspread with a nice duvet. Get rid of the VCR (who needs it when there's DirectTV?), and replace the old TV with an LCD on a swing arm to make the awkwardly high position more easy to adjust and view. Add a programmable thermostat so that the fan isn't constantly running. Keep a better eye on the breakfast room so that things are well stocked and the tables aren't dirty and full of trash.Overall, the hotel was good but not great. It really is so close to being fantastic that the small things (and unfortunately there were many that really added up) took away from what could have been a perfect experience. I would definitely consider returning, though, mostly because of the unbeatable location and price.

<Author>Instep
<Content>Good Hotel....but not for all I enjoyed my stay at the Charlesmark. The staff were friendly and helpful, the bar interesting and lively. Some excellent features (for example, the free to use internet access) were a real boon.Of course, it was not perfect. I was travelling alone and had relatively little luggage but the rooms are not huge (a common issue in Boston hotels I think). I do think however that some of the design features were probably better on paper than when they were put into effect. For example, the 'wardrobe' is only desk high and pretty limited in space - so very little space for clothes if you do not travel light. The mini fridge really is mini (2 small bottles of water) which was fine for me but might be limiting for a thirsty famuily in on a hot summer day.The TV and surround sound were good but annoyingly there were no instructions on how to use them (many thanks to the helpful cleaning ladies!) and if you are not used to the particular system it is rather confusingLocation is great and lots to see and do around the hotel. My room faced Boylston but it did not seem to noisy to me.So if you travel light, like the modern feel and are not too bothered about space then a room at the Charlesmark is worth going for!

<Author>blackstar9
<Content>Romantic Weekend Spent the weekend in Boston in mid-February. Check in was quick, then up to our room on the 5th floor, front of the building, looking across to the public library. Rooms were decorated nicely, mood music playing. The view at night was nice as well. Getting to the hotel was easy, parked out front to register, then just a few blocks away to the recommended garage. The walk back is not bad, just stop at either a Dunkin Donuts or Starbuck along the way. The room was nicely appointed. Good bed, sheets, furniture. After a night on the town, got back to the hotel around 10pm, bar was busy, but could have found a seat if we wanted. We needed dessert, so doorman recommended the Cheesecake factory just a short walk away. Felt completely safe walking around at night. They offer coffee, juice, and donuts in the morning, just enough to get you moving. Room was quite, could not hear neighbors or street traffic. Overall, great stay, would stay there next time in Boston.

<Author>UM1997
<Content>Great location + great price= fantastic hotel! I was in town for a conference and all of the conference hotels were booked- since I used to live in Boston, I remembered the Charlesmark and was very pleased to not only find that they had rooms available, but to find out that their room rates were almost $100 less than the other area hotels!! We arrived early in the day and they let us check in early. It's true that the rooms are on the small side, but I found the space to be more than ample for just me. The room had a queen sized bed and a small pull out sofa. My bathroom was smaller because I was next to the elevator, but I was very happy with the slate tile and the large shower stall. My co-worker's bathroom was about 3X the size of mine, and he had a bathtub, but the trade off was that I had 2 huge windows overlooking the Boston Public Library while he had a window to the alley. Since I was right next to the elevator, I expected it to be loud throughout the night but was very surprised when it was quiet all night long. I love city noise, so I wasn't disturbed being right on busy Boylston St., but if you're not used to nighttime city noise, it might take some getting used to!I think one thing that we all loved was that the room is wired with surround sound and besides the Direct TV channels, it also has all of the music channels, so showering with music playing was a big hit for all of us! The hotel serves a small continental breakfast in the morning with fruit, bagels, muffins  donuts  instant oatmeal. There is also coffee  juice. Since I'm familiar with the area, I opted to grab breakfast elsewhere but I did bring it back and sat in the hotel's lounge to eat. The lounge is really nice and at night, turns into a very hip bar. It got pretty busy on the weekend but was still a nice chill place to relax.The Charlesmark's location can't be beat. You're right across from the Copley T stop and within walking distance of pretty much the entire city. I highly recommend this hotel. I know that when I come back to Boston, this is definitely where I will stay!

<Author>LauderDale12
<Content>This hotel missed the mark Upon arrival at the check-in desk I was told to move my luggage to the bar area and wait.Five minutes later, the receptionist, a young latino, told me he was ready.He checked me in, and told me my room was on the 1st floor (a euphemism for the basement).I took the elevator to the basement and found my room in a warren at the end of the hall.After an inspection of the room, the closet was one-foot wide and there was no storage for clothing,I decided to return to the receptionist and ask to visually inspect another room.I was taken to one of the upper floors, to a room overlooking Boylston Street and the Boston Public Library. It too, was postage stamp sized, but the view was better than the basement.I was informed (even though the room was made-up) that I would have to wait for them to ready the room. I waited in the lounge for about forty-five minutes, when I was told the room was ready.Up to this point, the receptionist was indifferent at best and at worst seemed as though he was being extremely taxed by my room change request. This seemed odd since I had seen no one else enter or leave the hotel since I arrived.The room was visually well-appointed, but to say it was small, is an understatement. There was a queen bed, a one-person sleeper sofa, a wall unit and two night stands. The clothes closet (3 feet high by 1 1/2 feet wide) was part of the wall unit. There was a storage cabinet in the base of the wall unit for suitcases, but there were no drawers at all. Shelving was part of the unit, so we put our toiletries and other non-clothing items on the shelves. If you want to take your clothes out of your luggage, you will be hard put to do so. The only other possible places are the night stands or two-coat hooks behind the entrance door.To give you an idea of how small the room was, when the sleeper was extended there was less than a foot between the end of the sleeper bed and the wall mirror. This made moving from the queen bed to the bathroom extremely difficult and one can only be amazed no one has fallen or been seriously injured with this set-up.The view from the room was excellent, but the only caveat is the noise factor. With the window facing the street one hears everything going on below. The hotel has patio in the front where chair and tables from the lounge spill out. When the lounge is in full swing at night, you can hear the music and the din of the revelers. In addition, we had a noise problem with the cleaning staff who always seemed to be chatting every morning outside our door.At check-out, I needed to leave my luggage while I went to lunch. Their luggage storage area is in the lounge under a counter, in full view of anyone passing by. They do put a cable through the straps, but since a divider separates the reception desk from the lounge, the security of the luggage is limited.In summary,The receptionist at check-in was apathetic and not very pleased to be of assistance. We felt his behavior was unprofessional and set a poor tone at our arrival.The rooms are postage stamp sized and not recommended for families or people with any physical limiations.The proximity of the lounge is problematic at night since noise is a major problem.The luggage storage is in an open area so security is limited.The location is good and very close to the Copley station on the Green Line.

<Author>DartmouthTravels
<Content>Not for people with cars! The two best things about this hotel are 1- price, and 2- location. The hotel, right across the street from the Boston Public Library and Copley Square, leaves the traveler right in the heart of Boston. Public transportation (the T) is located only steps from the front door, and the Charlesmark benefits from many nearby restaurants.While other travelers claim the Charlesmark is designed in modern style, I felt I could do similar work in my dorm room with a trip to Ikea. The hotel is clean, but I actually felt that $139 was more than I should have paid for my queen bed room overlooking Boylston street/ the library. There is surround sound music (even in the bathrooms), and the bed was quite comfortable. The shower didn't always offer hot water.For location and price, it works...but one should not expect anything extraordinary. Furthermore, because we paid $32 for parking, we didn't really feel like we saved much from having chosen the Charlesmark. In the end, we thought it was a funny experience and something unlike what we would normally choose. I would probably pay around $200 next time to get parking and a much-upgraded room nearby.

<Author>JF945
<Content>Excellent Hotel The Charlesmark Hotel is an excellent, small hotel. It only has 33 rooms and it's in a great location in Boston. I do live in the greater Boston area but some friends come up annually for a convention. We found this hotel 3 years ago and it was a great find. Rates are less than the larger hotels in Boston. If you are looking for a pool, health club, though, this is not the place for you. The Charlesmark doesn't have either of these amenities but they do have agreements with a health club in the area for use if you are so inclined. There is free internet in the common area as well as continental breakfast each morning. The breakfast has tea, coffee, hot chocolate, fruit, muffins, bagels, juice. The lower level (basement) has a microwave and ice machine. During the day, the bar isn't open and it becomes a place to sit and read the paper or watch TV. The large common area also has comfortable seating and at night this area doubles as a club. It is up a few stairs and one night there was a private party up there. The steps made it easy for the management to close it off for the private event. Each room has toiletries, iron/ironing board, hair dryer, CD/DVD player. Our room for 3 had a double bed and a twin sleep sofa with wall shelves and an armoire with plenty of storage.The only thing the rooms lack is a refrigerator. Bottles of water are placed in the room but it would be nice if they were cold. A small cube fridge in each room would make it perfect. We will definitely stay here again.

<Content>Great time at Charlesmark I stayed at the Charlesmark Hotel Nov. 17-Nov. 20 for a conference. I choose the Charlesmark based on location and the good reviews on Tripadvisor. <Author>wellsf
<Content>Wonderful Experience We had never been to Boston before so didn't know what a wonderful area Back Bay is. We were less than 100 metres from Copley underground station in a really nice area of town. Close to some great restaurants. Our favourite, again only 100 metres down the same street, was the Atlantic Fish Co where we went twice in 6 nights. the service and food were excellent for the price. The staff in the hotel were always pleasant and helpful. The entrance contains a small reception desk and a very tidy cocktail bar which spills out onto the street with umbrellas. Up a few stairs at the back is the lounge/breakfast room with 2 consoles for free fast internet access. the breakfasts were bagels, muffins, fruit, fruit juice and hot drinks...perfectly adequate whilst you read the complimentary newspapers. The basic room we had was not big, if you've been to New York you will understand. But it was very tidy with Sky sports which was handy for the World Series ( GO SOX). Considering the area and the price we paid I would say the Charlesmark is a giveaway. I have no hesitation but to recommend it very highly. If I go back to Boston I won't be looking elsewhere for a hotel.

<Author>Travelwalker2
<Content>Great location but expensive for what it is. This boutique hotel is nice on the inside and a bit hidden from view but the noise on Boylston St can keep you awake at night. It is very close to access to the T and other city attractions. Our room had a nice contemporary decor and it was very clean. The front desk staff was not attentive and on one ocassion we were given incorrect directions to a nearby store. They did not great us when we entered or left the building; they were more interested in the computer than the guests! For the price ($230./night+) they should provide: glass (not plastic) wine and drinking glasses in the room; a small fridge other than the mini water fridge which made a lot of noise and 1 extra set of towels (just in case they are needed). The continental breakfast was probably the worst I have ever had. Package oatmeal, donuts, bagels, apples and oranges, coffee and Lipton tea. Not even a thank you when we left with our $800.00 bill. Suggest they work on their customer relations or lower the room rates to reflect what they should charge for the poor service and food.

<Author>hellothere_7
<Content>Charlesmark-Perfect for 20-30 something couples My boyfriend and I came to Boston from Kansas City for a long weekend and stayed at the Charlesmark in September and it was perfect for us! We stayed on the 4th floor and didn;t have any problems with noise at night. The hotel was immaculate and trendy, with a cool bar. The showers as everyone has said are fantastic! Awesome location--one block from Newbury St and directly across the street from the Copley Square T stop, which is super simple to get around on. Get a pass for $15 for 7 days at the airport and use it unlimited for the duration of your stay, including to and from the airport. I would highly reccommend this hotel, to anyone who is looking for a cool hotel in a great location.

<Author>kevnord
<Content>Great, Hip Hotel with unhelpful staff The Charlesmark is within a few blocks of Copley Place, Boston Commons, and Newbury Street.The room I had was great, oozing with style. My room looked out on the very busy Boylston street but was extremely quiet. The only negative thing I have to say about the hotel is in regards to the staff. Every time I interacted with them, I was made to feel as though I was bothering them. The only interactions I had were checking in and out. Lame.If you checking before your room is available, they will hold your luggage for you. However, they do not have a room for luggage and instead store it in the bar, under a counter. They run a wire through the handle and lock it up, but it's still out in the open. There are two computers attached to the internet downstairs, very handy.All-in-all, I would stay at this hotel again. The room/location were nice enough to make me overlook the rude staff members I encountered.

<Content>It Was As We Hoped It Would Be Taking the train from Penn Station in NYC left us just a 5 minute walk from the hotel. <Author>obxwahoo
<Content>Pretty Good Place We flew up to Boston to spend time in the city and visit old friends, and booked one night here and the next night with our friends. Many high points: great location, very unique decor, not your everyday chain hotel. Sure the rooms are small, but it didn't really bother us. Nice touches: Surround sound system in the room that also plays in the bathroom, Direct TV and music (which was set to classical as we entered our room), light (but tasty) breakfast, friendly service. The bathroom was terrific - made of stone and slate and great water pressure - I want one at home. The bar is happening at night, so book a room on floor two or above if noise bothers you. The few lows: the TV remote is a bear to operate (it changes channels, but does not successfully control the sound on the receiver), no closet in the room (cabinets instead), the Internet was down in the lobby while we were there. Otherwise, a great stay at a very reasonble cost. You won't be disappointed.

<Author>AcademicTraveler37
<Content>Good value, Good location, happy with stay I stayed at the Charlesmark for one night, as I was doing some research at Harvard. The price was the best available (I paid $169.00 on Orbitz) and the location, as others have said, can't be beat--right on Boylston Street, across from Library and one-two blocks from Copley Place and other shopping. 1/2 block from the T stop. I agree that the rooms are really small--mine was 604, and I agree with the person who stayed in 504 that this is probably the smallest room on each floor, so consider that when you check in. I also agree that there was some sort of background noise that I couldn't get rid of--probably the A/C outside. Finally, I could see the bar was very trendy and popular for the elite Boston set, and that may appeal to some people, but for me it just clogged the lobby (which is TINY) and made me feel like the conspicuously alone, unhip traveler that I am.BUT the room was new, spotless, very comfortable, and had free bottled water, scads of TV channels, free local phone calls, and a stereo w/CD changer, if you like to listen to music. There was also a guide to Boston in the room--not a magazine, but an actual guidebook--for us during one's stay. I've not seen that at other hotels. I found the staff very friendly and appreciated the free internet in the lobby (though it was in high demand, and one of the two computers was broken). overall I highly recommend the hotel for single travelers, esp on short stays, who like to be centrally located and who don't need a lot of space (and who like trendy digs).

<Author>DNaada
<Content>Pleasant Boutique Hotel Spent one night at the Charlesmark.Positives: Excellent location in the Back Bay area of Boston, one block off of Newbury St and good shopping. Service was good, with a modest but adequate continental breakfast (bagels, muffins, apples and bananas,) ,included in the rate. The bathroom ws small but nicely tiled. They allowed us an early check-in, with the room available by 11am. They had a good selection of TV stations (including several HBO channels), and they provided free bottled water in a mini-chiller.Negatives: The room was small, and instead of the promised 2 beds, there was one full-size bed and a fold-out twin sofa. It was difficult to control the temperature in the room, so it was always too hot or too cold. The sink area was quite small. The TV had very poor volume control, with a difficult to operate remote control. It was a CRT TV. There was no refrigerator/mini-bar in the room.

<Author>Tobinyon
<Content>Great stay at the Charlesmark Just got back from a weekend in Boston, Friday August 17 thru Sunday August 19, 2007 and stayed at the Charlesmark Hotel. Excellent location and very easy to get to off the Green line T at Copley. The hotel is lively and is very small but if you are there visiting for the weekend or for a few days, I would recommend this hotel. Right across from the Boston library and just down from Copley Square where the Westin and Fairmont hotels are, you can't beat the price and location. There isn't much of a lobby, most of it is the bar but they do have an upper lounge area with 2 workstations offering free internet access. The hotel does offer free continental breakfast which was just fine for us consisting of coffee, OJ, hot water  teas/hot chocolate, fresh bagels with cream cheese or butter or jelly, fresh fruit and a variety of fresh muffins and pastries. Up in the room they list the places nearby where you can get a full breakfast if you prefer that. We stayed on the 4th floor in a queen room, for I heard that it could be noisy on the first floor and I could see why because Boyolston street is hopping along with the bar downstairs all night long.Our room, 403 was a good size providing all the amenities one needs. The view consisted of looking into an alley but we were not there for the view. Bathroom was large with a cold slate floor and shower area. Great toiletries of shampoo, conditioner, mouthwash and lotion (no body wash). Not much counter space but enough for 2 people. The hotel is fun with a modern flair and we found service to be great. On Sunday we checked out in the AM and the hotel held our bags until our flight in the evening for no charge.Back Bay area was great, close to the Prudential Center shops, Top of the Hub and lots of great bistros and landmarks for sight seeing. There is a restaurant next to the Charlesmark bar called Bangkok Blue and is actually the one who does the food for the hotel's patio area out front. We dined there for a late lunch and they offer Thai food. We eat alot of Thai food and we give this restaurant a very high recommendation for the excellent food we ate.The hotel isn't far from Fenway park for we could hear the crowds during the games and the area was very busy in the afternoons and evenings but you felt safe walking around.After seeing most of Boston over the past 2 days and feeling beforehand that if you could afford it that you should really stay down at the waterfront for a great visit, there are more advantages to staying in Back Bay. You are right in the middle of everything and can spend less for a hotel room versus nearer the waterfront. We highly recommend this hotel and would consider staying at the Charlesmark again.  
<Date>Aug 20, 2007

<Author>Michele13
<Content>Superb boutique hotel, great value This hotel is such a find in Boston, where it's hard to get a quality hotel under $200/night. I had an upgraded room (at $189/night) which had a large window overlooking Bolyston Street and the Boston Public Library. Though my room was on the second floor, overlooking the busy street and over the bar, it was extremely quiet. The room was very nice and just how others have described -- with a great sound system, gigantic floor-to-ceiling mirror that made the room look bigger, and a TV with tons of channels. My room didn't have a traditional desk and chair, so don't count on having a lot of formal work space. The bar has great outdoor seating, and was usually crowded during my stay. Breakfast was continental, with bagels, doughnuts, fruit, and oatmeal, too, I believe. Although not overly friendly, I found the front desk staff extremely helpful. They helped me navigate my way via T to the new convention center, and one stood outside during a rainstorm to hail me a cab. The 2 computers in the breakfast area were a nice touch.

<Author>Voyageurchic
<Content>Rude or indifferent, you decide We just returned from a fantastic time in New England. I had returned to walk the state of my birth. Our only disappointment during our entire stay was with the Charlesmark Hotel. We generally choose boutique hotels when we celebrate...it was my birthday on the day we arrived. My husband had emailed the hotel-with little interest on recommending ways to make it special. We arrived already in awe of the city to be greeted with a lowered head at reception that did not raise and a monotoned...'Name'. My cheerfulness plummeted, but not detered. Perhaps this is 'uber chic indifference'...but it carried on throughout our stay. To my mind, it became rudeness. We dropped our bags and went down for a drink, 15 minutes early... the bartender was chatting with the receptionist-'not open' again, not interested. As a former actor in New York and therefore bartender. I was disappointed in their disinterest in their customers. I certainly would have offered an alternative to a couple that had just arrived from 14 hours of travel... A true reflection of our entire three nights...they were more interested in gossip than service...which was reflected in the conversation of fellow guests on our final morning. The room was small but accurately represented on their website. The bathroom was great with a terrific shower. In fact, once you made it past the cool indifferent corridors of reception, you could not fault the stay. The donuts and bagels in the morning were fresh and the coffee a perfect start for the day. I wouldn't go there again, which is too bad, as we will be in Boston several times a year...it would have been nice to find a place to come back 'where everybody knows your name'...but I am certain they had no idea or interest in who we were.

<Author>Cville_Sojourner
<Content>Loved the Charlesmark Just got back from Boston. Our stay at the Charlesmark was excellent. The staff was very welcoming and helpful. We stayed on the 6th floor in a queen room. Walked in, and light jazz was playing on the full Audio-Visual system (even had speakers in the bathroom). Room was good sized, done in a modern motif: built-in bookcase, european lights. Bath a little small, no tub, but a large shower. Bed was fine, room might be on the dark side for some. No street noise, and quiet, even though we were right at the elevator. No view from the windows (but we don't really care about that).The downstairs lounge was very nice, and the sidewalk cafe pleasant.The location is the thing! Walk out the door and see the public library, look diagonally across and see Trinity Church. A couple of steps and you are on the T. . . Would definitely recommend!

<Author>unfrequentflyer
<Content>Great location. good value for Boston The location of this hotel is unbeatable. The metro (or T) brings you to the doorstep from the airport. It is located opposite the Public Library and is within walking distance to most sights including Boston Common and the start of the Freedom Trail. There are also good dining options around the hotel. I booked a single room and although on the slightly small side, it was very compactly appointed and extrememly stylish. The bed was comfortable and the sheets etc were spotlesssly clean. There was a large full length mirror on one of the walls which helped to give an impression of having a larger room. The TV had an amazing selection of channels and the CD player/radio was connected to a cery high quality sound system which included speakers in the bathroom too. Speaking of which the bathroom was comparatively large and the power shower excellent. What I particularly enjoyed was to take a long luxurious shower with the music of Mozart piped into the bathroom!My room did not have a view to speak of but that didn't bother me. With respect to the staff, I woujld say that the standard was more variable. upon arrival I was met by a really charming and enthusiastic receptionist who asked about my flight, and proceeded to give me helpful brochures and maps of Boston and tips on where to dine and visit etc. On the subsequent days I noticed that the receptionist was occasionally distant and somewhat aloof, but never rude. The breakfast was OK. Orange juice, muffins and bagels from Dunkin' Doughnuts, fairly good coffee, Philadelphia cream cheese, jam and fruit, instant oatmeal. On same days the breakfast started a little late as they still hadn't gotten the fresh supply of bagels, but its a small point. Bottled water was complimentary.For the price I think it was good value for Boston given its outstanding location and quality of the rooms, considering tat breakfast is included. I would stay again if ever I were to return to Boston.

<Author>Paka68
<Content>Small but Great! If you can handle a small room this is a wonderful place to stay. We really enjoyed the three nights we spent here and the location is excellent. We had a rental car but just left it parked at the garage because the hotel is so close to everything. The parking fee was reasonable for the area, $20 for 24 hours but keep in mind that applies from noon to noon and be sure to get the written directions on how to get to the garage (less than 10 minute walk) because the hotel is not very good at explaining it.The room was very nice as was the bathroom with it's Italian granite. The closet was a joke, totally unusable because it was so small. If you need to hang things, especially full length items do not stay here. The furniture was very nice, comfortable bed and a great sound system with speakers throughout the room and bathroom. It was very clean. The room wasn't too bad in size, it was just the bathroom and closet that were way too small.Front desk service was quite good (except for garage directions) and they were very considerate. The continental breakfast fell short, not much of a selection, pretty minimal.Overall we would definitely recommend this hotel and stay there again... just remember - small is the operative word.

<Author>ingrdo
<Content>Really, really overrated After reading reviews on tripadvisor, in magazines, Boston's Best of...about the Charlesmark, I decided to book it. I think this place and its staff have let the reviews go to their collective head. For paying $198 per night, I expected a lot more in terms of customer service. When I walked in, there were three people behind the 2.5 foot long front desk. Two continued their personal conversation and the third person looked at me with no interest whatsoever. There was no How may I help you?. No good afternoon. No nada. When I asked for help with our bags, one young man followed me out to the car and watched as I unloaded the bags. It took over one-half hour for our bags to make it to our room. Although there was an apology offeredfor it taking so long, it was given while the offeror was on his cellphone in the midst of a personal conversation. This was not a good sign. None of the three staff we had regular contact with would engage in a conversation without being prompted, no good morning, etc. The carpets did not appear to have been vaccumed either in the halls or our room in several days. Again, not for essentially $200 a night. There are some positives: The interior design is great, there is one bartender named Jefferson who I'd recommend to anyone, the location is perfect (however, any downtown hotel is strategically located for business/tourist travel), the disorganization and generalinattention to detail got us a couple glasses of Pinot Noir and appetizers for free. That wasn't the intention, however. When I checked out, I was told that everything was taken care of. I remindedthe person at the desk that we had two nights of a bar tab charged toour room. She looked at me, said, Well, that's a separate system andhe (not sure who) isn't here right now. Twenty minutes later one ofthe staff said, Your charge is $10 but I'm having a hard time printing it. In the next ten minutes, he walked by me four times anddid not address me. While we were double parked and loading our car ourselves, I ran back in and asked that the bill be mailed to me. BTW, our bill should have been about $50 so I'm apparently as confused as they are. We'll be back in Boston in September and will not be staying here!

<Author>cmalloy
<Content>Stay only if you cannot beat the price I like Boston/Cambridge and have visited the city a lot. The Charlesmark is in a great location. However, I have paid much less or the same for much nicer accomodations also located in great locations. The Charlesmark is NOT worth what I paid: $200.00 approximately for each night. This price includes tax. 1) The rooms are very very small. They are clean but it is difficult to move around in them. Again, if the price had been less, I would have adjusted. The showers are tastefully tiled and the bathroom, overall, is quite nice. Warning: If you require a tub and are not handicapped, you will be sent to the rooms on the floor where the hotel restaurant's bathroom, laundry, and vending machines are located. Not visually appealing!2) The hallways are narrow and the carpet (outside the rooms) is stained and worn. The elevator has seen better days; I usually took the stairs. Overall, the hotel's appearance is slightly shabby. I do not refer to the rooms but to the lobby and hallways.3) The staff is a mixed lot. There are those who are helpful and those who are not. You will know them when you meet them.Bottom line: I stayed at the Inn at Harvard (lovely) after I left the Charlesmark. The difference in rooms, lobby, and atmosphere is stunning. Ironically, both places charged almost the same price. If you can get this place for a bargain rate, go for it. Otherwise, I wouldn't waste my time. There are so many better places to stay.

<Author>Freischutz
<Content>Outstanding small hotel The Charlesmark Hotel could not be better situated. In the heart of Boston's Back Bay directly above the Copley Square subway station, it's in easy walking distance of the whole of the centre of the City. The hotel has recently undergone a major refurbishment and, although the rooms are small (even by European standards), they are very well appointed. The bathrooms are particularly noteworthy: the slate finish is not only very practical but also very attractive. The room in which we stayed had a double bed and a sofabed. We used both. The sofabed - never the most rest-inducing pieces of furniture - was of decent quality and totally satisfactory for the three night duration of our stay. The inclusive continental breakfast was a plus, as was the free internet access from terminals in the breakfast/upper bar area.If arriving in the city by air, ignore the blandishments of the Transit Authority to catch the silver line bus from Logan Airport into the centre. Instead, take the airport shuttle #33 from the terminal to the blue line subway station, changing to the green line at Government Centre station. The journey from the airport terminal to the hotel front desk by this route will take you no more than 30 minutes. If arriving in the city by Amtrak from the South, the hotel is barely 5 minutes' walk from the Back Bay train station.

<Author>ZipZoo
<Content>Excellent value, excellent service For a 3-day conference at Hynes Convention center, I turned to TripAdvisor to find a hotel nearby that would fit the budget of my employer. I contacted the Charlesmark directly and made a reservation, which was confirmed promptly by e-mail and gave directions to the municipal parking lot where they've arranged a $20 discounted rate, much better than the Prudential Center's $36 a night. On arrival in Boston I parked my car, then stopped in at the Charlesmark on the way to the Hynes and left my bag. When I returned that night, my bag had already been nicely placed in my room. While the room was not large, it was quiet, the contemporary decor was attractive and the space well utilized. Bottles of water were left in the room each day at no charge, there was a stereo, video player, cable TV, and a huge full length mirror. Two computer stations with internet are available in the downstairs lounge. In the morning, there are newspapers, juice, coffee, fruit, bagels and so on, all included in the room rate. Coffee and pretzel-type snacks are available throughout the day. The staff was quite helpful and I was very pleased with the hotel. Those traveling for pleasure might want to ask about room views--my room had a very limited rear view, which was fine for me, but might not work for everyone. This is a nice area for visitors, with plenty of shopping and restaurants nearby on Boylston Street and in the Prudential Center Mall. It's an easy walk to Newbury Street and to the Boston Common, there's a Shaw's Supermarket nearby , and a Green Line subway stop on the corner.

I heard that the room I was going to recieve was one that is in the lower level with no windows or view. I ask them to change the room, because I have a problem being in a room with no windows, well they gave me a Queen size room on an upper floor with a view for the same price of $149.00 the price of a double bed room. The Charlesmark is a Wonderful place to stay, the rooms are super clean, the shower is amazing -great water pressure, the lolipops in the toothbrush holders are really cute, free internet service in the lobby , free bottled water, and free continental breakfast. There is a bar downstairs and it is a little noisy, but just get a room on one of the upper floors and you will be fine. I so loved staying here, I would reccommed this hotel to anyone going to boston. The Charlesmark is GREAT !!!

<Author>glencora
<Content>Terrific Hotel in Copley Square We've just returned from 2 nights in Boston, where we stayed at the Charlesmark on Boylston Street in Copley Square. It is a wonderful small hotel. We were able to park outside the hotel while we checked in. Longer term parking was simple and reasonable, being about 4 blocks from the hotel in municipal parking. The parking garage exited almost directly onto Route 90, which made our departure (even at rush hour) quick and seamless. We had a beautiful, contemporary (if small) room overlooking the Boston Public Library. The bathroom was clean and new. There was high quality audio equipment, satellite tv and wireless internet service in the room. Breakfast was included in the room rate and was basic (rolls, muffins, coffee) but good. There was a bar in the lobby from whom we purchased a bottle of wine for our room. The employees were young, polite and very helpful. I wouldn't hesitate to return to the hotel.

<Author>elisaNorway
<Content>Good hotel experience I stayed at the Charlesmark for almost one week in March 2007. I had read the reviews about the small rooms, but got a good rate so I decided to stay there anyway. I'm glad I did. The location is perfect, practically walking distance to anywhere in the city. The standard of the room was also good, and the room was definately big enough for 1 person. The bathroom and shower was nice. Some negative things to mention though: 1)There was not a proper full size hanging closet. Since I was travelling on business I brought several suits and dresses, and I had to hang these on a hook in the bathroom in lack of other alternatives. 2) very dim light in the room. (I like getting dressed in a room where I can actually see the color of the clothes I'm wearing) Since there was nothing but a brick wall outside the window, no real daylight came into the room and the lamps were not very strong. On the positive side though, I loved the huge dressing mirror!3) Breakfast was very very basic. (But it was complimentary...)Summed up: the hotel is definately worth checking out, just be aware of the few things I mentioned above...(I could very well just be more picky than the average guest :-)

<Author>tritravel
<Content>Overall Good We came away with a good experience at this hotel although it did not start well. We arrived at 5:30 pm for our 1 night stay and were sent to our queen-bed room -- only to find that it had not yet been cleaned from the previous guests. Towels on the floor, window wide open, generally a mess. We went back down to get a different room, and the guy at the front desk was not very helpful, friendly, or apologetic (his first offer was for us to wait while he ran and cleaned the room for us, even though we had told him we needed to shower and get on our way for an appointment). Finally we got a different, smaller room with a better view, and we were told we could discuss a discount the next morning with a manager. The room we booked should have cost $139, and they put us in a $119 room. We were told the lowest they could go on discount was $99. The next morning the manager offered a discount down to $99, and when we checked out, there was an envelope with $40 in cash waiting for us, since we had prepaid for the room through hotels.com. This was great for our good will!The hotel itself was very nice, and the lounge and bar were fun. Everything was clean and the stereo system and speakers in the room and bathroom were great. We will definitely go back and stay again -- the location and price can't be beat. It's a funky hotel with nice atmosphere. We will bring our own pillows next time, though -- the ones they provided were pretty limp.

<Author>CBJBSouthCarolina
<Content>Great place to stay in Boston! Came to Boston to attend a conference at the Hynes Convention Center...Although not directly connected to the center like the Sharaton or Marriot, the CharlesMark was only a few minutes walk away with a Dunkin Donuts and Starbucks (whichever you prefer) along the way. The rooms were exactly the right size for a single traveler or couple without children, and the showers were heaven...lots of water pressure and beautiful stonework. The ambient music in the rooms was also a plus. I loved to relax in the the lounge in the evenings and check my e-mail or search the web. There are plenty of excellent restaurants within a block or 2 of the hotel, especially if you enjoy steaks, seafood, or asian/sushi. There is also a LOT of great shopping within walking distance, if you are so inclined. We did not utilize the T system on this trip, but the Copley station is within a block. The front desk staff were very helpful as was one of the owners, who interacted with the customers on a regular basis. I would highly recommend this Hotel for any visit to Boston.

<Author>ExtraPickles
<Content>Best Value in Boston's Back Bay When I booked a room at the Charlesmark for $129 per night, I was nervous. How could a new hotel in the heart of Boston's Back Bay be so affordable? After spending a night there, I am still asking that question ... for it was a clean, stylish hotel in a prime location with a room rate that is at least $50 cheaper than anything else I've found in the area.As promised, the front desk attendant told me that we'd have a quiet room on the sixth floor (room 606). The room was designed in a contemporary style similar to West Elm. Design was also functional, allowing for maximum room in a tight space. For example, here was no minifridge; instead, there was a minicooler on a media case shelf that held two free bottles of spring water. Keep in mind that this room spacewise is fine for two people, but you'll have to upgrade to the hotel鈥檚 larger room type for a party of three. The in-room TV had hundreds of channels, including Fox Sports stations for at least a dozen regional areas (ex. Arizona, Pittsburgh). XM music channels were also available through the TV ... and broadcast into the bathroom with an adjustable volume control.The bathroom had a stone-like decor and featured a good assortment of amenities, including two lollipops in the toothbrush holder. The water had great pressure and almost instantly adjusted to my preferred temperature preferences.Incredibly, the room rate includes a continental breakfast in the lounge. Several newspapers were available to read as we munched on bagels, fresh fruit, and oatmeal.The attendant was the only staffperson we saw during our stay; she was polite and showed me a larger room upon my request (I was curious to see what the extra money would've gotten us). The size of the rooms made me question the accessibility of the lodging options, but she informed me that there are two accessible rooms on the property.The style of the Charlesmark makes it great for romantics and hipsters, while the price and location of the hotel is a rare find for families and budget travelers. I need to find an excuse to return!

<Content>Charlesmark was fantastic We had such a terrible vacation in Boston, picking all the wrong things to see on their most crowded days. The one bright spot of our trip was the Charlesmark. It must cost half the price of the hotels just across Copley but we wouldn't know based on the quality of our stay. Our (little) room was SO comfortable and just big enough for two. We had one of the rooms with the double beds and were impressed with how economically space was used. We had a fantastic view of a brick wall -- literally -- but felt very secluded from the hustle and bustle of the streets below because we were all the way at the back of the hotel (room 205, FYI). Lobby staff was standoffish but, hey, it's Boston. Everyone seemed freakin' miserable. And anyway, I called downstairs several times to get phone numbers and information and received it promptly and politely. The shower was INCREDIBLE -- we're talking about it still two weeks later -- and the little perks like strategically placed speakers, satellite TV and radio and a bar right downstairs couldn't be beat. Plus, there were computers for us to use and print our boarding passes when we were ready to get the heck out of town already.

<Author>Mooch_1013
<Content>Great location, good value, memorable stay! My girlfriend and I just got back from two nights at the Charlesmark. I was looking to stay somewhere centrally located, relatively inexpensive, and above all, memorable. The Charlesmark delivered in all of these areas.First, as others have noted, the location can't be beat. From the Charlesmark, if you walk at a decent pace, it's 30 seconds to a T stop, 45 seconds to the Boston Public Library, 3 minutes to the Trinity Church, Copley Plaza, or Newbury Street, and 5 minutes or so to the Boston Public Garden. BTW, the Parish Cafe (361 Boylston St.) had maybe the best sandwiches I've ever had in my life.Second, it's relatively cheap. $129 for the regular room, and $30 more for a slightly larger room. We stayed in a regular room on the top (6th) floor, but took a peek into one of the larger rooms while it was being cleaned. If you're extremely claustrophobic, maybe you'll want to get the larger room, but otherwise, you should probably save your money.Third, it was memorable. When we first opened the door to the room, my impression was My god, this room is small. But as we unpacked, and I started discovering the nice little touches around the room that make the absolute optimally-efficient use of the limited amount of space, I became more and more impressed. For example, most hotels I've stayed at have had a big dresser and a closet. Here, there were drawers that were concealed at the bottom of the foot of the platform-style bed, and sets of drawers to the sides of the headboard of the bed. There's a cabinet in the bottom of the AV-unit where you can hang clothes, and places to hang coats behind the door. The AV-unit also had a cabinet perfectly sized to hold a large carry-on bag, and a space at the top for a suitcase. Dimming lamps folded against the headboard of the platform bed. Also, there was a huge (7 ft or so tall by 4 ft wide) mirror against the wall, next to the window, creating the illusion of more space.Now, I'm a city-dweller writing from a relatively small condo in the heart of a city, so the Charlesmark hit a number of my sweet spots as far as preferences. In fact, I'm impressed with the layout and use of space to the point that I'm going to try to steal some of the elements of their design for my own place. However, I can see how someone with different tastes might feel a bit cramped in a Charlesmark room. If having a hotel room large enough to throw a football around in is your thing, then you'd probably be better off somewhere else. But if you want somewhere that's well-located, relatively cheap, and memorable, you might want to try the Charlesmark.  
<Date>Dec 4, 2006
