<Author>TravelDealer
<Content>Perfect hotel, too bad about the staff... After taking a tour of the Charlesmark last June, we decided to have the members of our wedding party stay there. We couldn't reserve a block of rooms because of the hotel size, so, we just had everyone call. Last June we had a great guy who offered to walk us around, show us rooms, etc. He sold us. Then came October...A few nights before checking in we swung by to check on our reservation. The kid behind the desk was initially less then helpful. When I asked if it was possible for all of the girls to be on one floor and the guys to be on another, he exhaled and said that it would be a real problem and we should have notified him earlier. When we noticed that some of our wedding party members hadn't made reservations, I said that we would call them and have them confirm. The kid behind the desk mis-heard us to say that we wanted him to call and confirm our reservations and responded with, That would be an absolute hassle for me to call everyone... which I immediately had to correct him to say that _we_ were going to call our friends. He seemed relieved. After asking for something else and getting denied, I left wondering if it was too late to go somewhere else. (By the time we checked in, the girls all did end up on the same floor with the guys on the two floors above) We checked in on the Wed before our Sat wedding. That's when we met Ingrid. She was the absolute shining star. She came to the rescue when our inquiries of can we have a late checkout on the day of the wedding were answered with (by someone else) I don't know that that's possible with a plethora of reasons why not. Ingrid said not to worry, she'll make it happen. Anytime anyone in our wedding party needed anything at all, she was there to help. Every one in the wedding party (even those who weren't able to get in because they were full) loved her. Unfortunately so did the Head of Human Resources at Tiffany's who's hired her for bigger and better things. Anyway, aside from the remaining staff, the hotel itself is quite nice. The bar area and lounge behind the bar are great. There's also free internet which is wonderful. The regular sized room is a bit small with only a half size closet. The refrigerator is only large enough for 2 bottles of water. We had to plug ours in only to find it unplugged by house keeping later. Normally we don't need a lot of space, so, a room that size is fine. We didn't find the drawers in the room until we left (they're under the bed). The double room is a better bet if you're rooming up with friends. There is a breakfast put out - donuts, bagels, water, and coffee. Although we didn't have time to hang out at the bar, all of our friends did and really loved it. It was definitely hopping at night. Overall I would recommend staying here if you don't normally talk to the front desk anyway. That is, if you're low maintenance. We usually are, but, due to the wedding we had a few more needs then the average customer. I know without a doubt if it wasn't for Ingrid, we would have been a lot worse off. All of that being said, we probably would stay here again at the location was fantastic and the price is definitely right.

<Author>Rodrir
<Content>Fantastic hotel! The Charlesmark Hotel was reasonably priced compared to other hotels in the area (it's in the Back Bay area -- great location). It's in the center of everything -- across the street from the Boston Library, close to the Fairmont Copley Hotel, the subway system, Boston Common, Prudential shopping center and many areas to eat. The rooms were small, but it's alright if you just want to come back to your hotel, rest and kick back. They provide upgrade/premium cable channels, including all the HBO channels. It's clean and everything seems new (looks like they just renovated the hotel.) In each room, they provide you with a great tourist guide book to borrow during your stay, if you want to take it with you when you check out from the hotel it's $14. There is no restaurant in the hotel but many in the area. You can order from a list provided to you by the hotel and they will deliver to your room. There is a gym close by that gives all the Charlesmark customers a discount; will charge $10 to allow you to use the gym. Their continental breakfast is great and you must have their bagels. They have have free internet service in their lobby floor. The only thing is they don't have parking and you must park your car two short blocks away for $35 a day.

<Author>HeatherHC
<Content>Great location, but bring earplugs My husband and I stayed in the Charlesmark on a Saturday night in October. The absolute best thing about this hotel is the location -- it's right down the street from a T stop, it's within easy walking distance of the Prudential Center (an indoor mall) and local restaurants, and the area (Back Bay) can't be beat for shopping, restaurants, nightlife, etc. We also loved the design -- everything was sleek and beautiful. Check-in was a breeze. Even though our room was not ready, they held our bags and then took them to our room for us. We were too excited to see Boston to want to be in our room anyway. The staff was young and very welcoming. We had a standard room on the first floor. We did not mind the size at all. There was very little walking room around the bed area, and only one person can comfortably fit in the bathroom, but everything seemed new. There are speakers above the shower, so you can listen to music while showering! The orange lollypops were a nice touch. I also liked the large, full-length mirror. Here is my gripe: There are two rooms on the ground floor through a door and down a short hallway from the very noisy bar. Since we were staying on a Saturday night and I had read the reviews on this site, I knew I didn't want to be on the ground floor by the bar. So I specifically asked to be above the ground floor. This did not happen. We were stuck in one of the two rooms on the ground floor, despite my request. I tried not to be too disgruntled, as we were too tired from our long journey to make a fuss. Needless to say, it was VERY loud back there. We could hear laughing and loud music well past midnight. However, having read the reviews on this site, I came prepared with earplugs and slept soundly.This is a lovely hotel in a great location. But be smart and bring those earplugs. You never know what floor you're going to end up on --and it could be 5 feet away from a noisy bar crowd.

<Author>dooper
<Content>Great location, good value... We have just returned from our first ever trip to the USA. we had a three week itinerary part of which included two night stopoever in Boston. After reading reviews, we choose the Charlesmark. The hotel is well located and its an easy walk to all those places you want to see. We had travelled by train from NYC and the hotel is only a short walk from the Amtrak station.The hotel is of the informal boutique variety and also has a public ground floor bar area. Reception was friendly and welcoming and we were assigned our standard room which was on a rear corner of the building on the fourth floor. Being on the corner meant we had two windows which gave a feeling of extra space to the rather small room size which others have commented on but is perhaps what is to be expected in a busy City. Having said that, they have made the best use of the space and the room and bathroom are clean, comfortable and well equipped and should suit most people for a stay of upto two or three nights.A continental breakfast is provided but some may decide that it isnt worth bothering with. Cooked breakfast can be had at keen prices at local eateries and the hotel recognises this in its room literature. The lounge area has two internet terminals for those essential emails home to friends and family.All in all a good value comfortable hotel in a great ,convenient location.

<Author>travelerinva
<Content>Great boutique hotel in the heart of Copley Square My husband and I recently stayed at the Charlesmark hotel. We had read the reviews (and compared prices) of all of the hotels in the Copley Square area and picked this one accordingly. We were not disappointed! The Charlesmark is a boutique hotel perfect for couples and single people looking for a great location and a very clean comfortable room; the rooms and bathrooms are very small so I would not recommend more than 2 people in a room. The decor is modern and trendy--flat screen tv, great stereo system (played music even in the bathroom!), free bottled water in the room. The bed was comfortable and the room was quiet even though we were put in the room right above the bar on the lobby level. The free continental breakfast consisted of fruit, coffee, juice, bagels, muffins and doughnuts from Dunkin' Doughnuts (I think there was also some instant oatmeal as well)--which was very nice and carefully attended to by the staff each morning.I would highly recommend this hotel for location, price, cleanliness and fun trendy atmosphere.

<Author>FlyMeToTheMoon
<Content>Clean, Stylish and Well-Located Gem The Charlemark is an excellent choice for anyone looking to stay in a fantastic, centrally-located spot in Boston without breaking the bank. I just returned from a 2-night visit there -- my first and only time staying here. I would return in a heartbeat, and will be thoroughly disappointed if it is not available for my next visit.The room itself was on the small side, but they made the most out of the space with an oversized mirror and shelves. There was a large flat screen tv with DirecTV, a stereo and a DVD player. The room was clean and my window happened to look out onto Boylston so I had a fantastic view of the public library and the entire Copley Square area.The staff was extremely polite and helpful. They made us feel welcome and helped answer all our questions, going out of their way to do so. The location can't be beat. The hotel sits directly across from the public library and the Copley T station. It's in the heart of back bay, with Newbury, Boston Common, Fanuiel Hall, Downtown Crossing, Chinatown all within walking distance. With the green line T stop right out your door, you can get to any other part of the city (Boston College, Harvard, the airport) with ease.I would recommend this hotel to anyone who likes boutique hotels -- this is not a roomy, luxurious chain-hotel room. It's modern, minimalist, and stylish, with small rooms and a funky feel to it. There is a lobby bar which spills out onto the street....you can dine and drink outside on Boylston. There is also inside lounge with a projector tv and two computers for hotel guests (with a printer as well). The continental breakfast consists of Dunkin Donut bagels and muffins, juice and coffee.I really enjoyed my stay here, as a 30-year old married woman visting with girlfriends. If you're looking for a quiet roomy place away from the hub-bub of the city, it may not be the place for you. At night, I had no trouble sleeping as the bar downstairs and outside traffic did not seep into the room at all, even with a window facing the street.

<Content>Great Place to Stay The Charlesmark, as others have said, is a very nice place to stay in an absolutely great location. I just returned this morning, and have nothing but good things to say. I wanted to post something on tripadvisor.com because I learned about the hotel on this website and very much appreciate having access to such a wealth of information before traveling. My room was very small, but the bed was comfortable, the pillows (four) were just right, every morning I was given two more water bottles (chilled), the air conditioning worked, the showers had good water pressure, the towels were soft, the breakfast (continental) was fresh and abundant, the internet was always available, my questions were answered with accurate and helpful information. I paid $169/night for a single. There is a pretty good Thai restaurant right next door. Oh, and the bar downstairs (that spills out onto the sidewalk when it's warm) is a happening place at night.Only drawback, and this isn't the hotel owners fault, is that my room backed up to an area that was very loud at about 2 in the morning with the extended noise of garbage being dumpted and with what sounded like 1 million beer/wine/booze bottles being poured into a dumpster. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Awesome staff, Exceptional overall From the moment we stepped into the door, the staff was very warm and helpful. Not only did the gentleman at the front desk help with our bags, but before we could retrieve more from the car he had already put them in the room for us! I've stayed at many 5-star and luxury hotels for business as well as pleasure over the years, but nothing comes close to the quality of service for what this boutique Hotel offers. Most of the staff are young, full of life and extremely familiar with local shops, sights and places to eat. The poor fellow that worked some nights couldn't have been more than 23, but couldn't have been more helpfull. When we asked for extra towels he was at the door almost as we put down the phone. What the rooms lack in terms of space the staff make up in friendliness. This is not a place where you come with the kids for a week, more like a personal and intimate getaway for a couple on a weekend or vacation. Call and ask questions, anyone that books a hotel should always be well informed as to what they are reserving. Nobody likes surprises. Here, you will find only pleasant ones. Thanks Charlesmark!

<Author>MyHobbyIsTravel
<Content>A gem in the heart of the city The hotel is a real gem. Boston's Back Bay is just out the front doorstep. It is located across the street from the Boston Public library and a few steps from Copley Square and the subway stop. The room I stayed in was compact but had everything I needed. Classical music, from the stereo system in the room, greeted me as I entered... which I thought was a nice touch. It was clean, stylish and quiet. The hotel provides tea and coffee in the evenings, and a light breakfast in the mornings. Computers are available for internet access, and wi-fi is available for those who have their own wi-fi compatible laptops. The hotel staff were very accommodating, pleasant, and informative. And the price can't be beat.... in such an expensive location, it is a great hotel for the cost. Anytime I'm in Boston in the future, The Charlesmark is where I'm going to stay.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Convenience is Right on the 'Mark' We agree with most of the previous posts. Our upgraded room on the second floor (201) was roomy enough but small by American standards. Size aside, the room and hotel has much going for it. Great view of the street from the windowsill (the marathon finish line is right outside). Direct TV provides lots of free channels and PPV movies. On top of that, the hotel offers a wide selection of free videos. Two PCs in the lounge provide FREE internet access 24/7. The staff was consistently friendly and helpful with all of our needs. Try the sour apple martini in the trendy little bar downstairs. For breakfast, unless you just want fruit, OJ and coffee, take a short walk up Boylston to Finagle a Bagel across from Copley Square. One of the best features for us was that the T stops were literally seconds from the Charlesmark's door. A walk of a few blocks in any direction will get you to the Prudential Center, Newberry Street, or the Public Gardens and Boston Common. Overall the Charlesmark is the epitome of convenience.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Stylish without breaking the bank Thought the Charlesmark was a very stylish hotel, and very reasonably priced for the area. We paid $199 per night for one of the larger rooms, which was adequately sized, and I found the decor and the furnishings to be very modern, and clean with no obvious wear and tear. I particularly liked the bathroom - it had a walk in shower, no bath, but everything was very stylish, with nice toiletries etc. The bar (which I believe has been recently renovated) was fabulous - all padded leather walls and plush seating. Really enjoyed the breakfasts - they were fairly basic, coffee, juice, bagels, pastries, fruit etc., - but they were excellent quality, and with newspapers and two internet points available to browse through, it made for a very pleasant start to the day. On our last day we decided to venture out to breakfast with a friend and on the recommendation of the hotel found a great value and wonderfully tasty breakfast in a bar a few blocks down Boylston Street. If you want style, good value, and a personal touch you don't get with the large chains, I would go for the Charlesmark every time.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Chic on the Cheap We stayed at the Charlesmark for three nights and it suited our purposes well. However, we are low maintenance travellers ie. Our needs are a good location (which it certainly is), clean, decent sized rooms, and generally somewhere quiet and safe to rest our heads. And the Charlesmark ticked those boxes. We were on the sixth floor in a Large category room, and it was quiet and clean with good air con and a big window and a v. small but extremely clean bathroom (Sorry, that should be shower room - as it did not have a bath). If you are a traveller who requires a bit more fussing over, and needs things like robes, ironing boards, room service and staff who'll run around after you, then the Charlesmark may not satisfy you. We found service friendly and fun, if not overly attentive. (We asked for some shirts to be pressed and eventually had to walk around the block to sort it out ourselves, when a requested ironing board never arrived). The breakfast, which is included in the price, was adequate if you just need a quick bite to start the day, and is served buffet style, so you certainly don't need to go hungry as there's plenty of it.Overall, good for those who spend most of their time out and about and just use their hotel as a sleeping/refuelling spot.

<Author>NapaNomad
<Content>Good hotel, good location We spent 3 nights at the Charlesmark the first week of May. I chose it from TripAdvisor reviews and was satisfied overall with the hotel. The hotel renovation and rooms are very clean, modern and comfortable; although quite small. The bathroom was standing room only for one to shower, brush teeth, etc.; but nicely done in stone tiles. We had a premium room with a queen bed and single sofa sleeper (little futon sofa). To me it is no frills accomodations; minimal space, minimal storage, tiny fridge that holds just 2 bottles of water (complimentary, daily). I would classify it as more of a business destination. The staff was aloof, but available. The lounge was full each evening; with patio seating on the street. There is plenty of great things to see and do right out the door and the subway is right on the same block. The hotel's continental breakfast is substantial enough. But trying to find a full breakfast, eggs, etc; within walking distance is a challenge. One morning we opted for the Westin Hotel's breakfast, about 2 blocks away. It was lovely and the tab was $50 (!)...on the last morning we disovered a great hide-away for breakfast at the Boston Public Library, downstairs off the courtyard. A small cafe with egg sandwiches, bagels, etc. Beats the Burger King.Bottomline, the cost of our room ($189 daily rate) was reasonable for the area, surrounding neighborhood is great and our top floor (6th) room was quiet. No real complaints.

<Content>Small but perfectly formed! My boyfriend and I stayed in the Charlesmark at the end of March for three nights. I think the hotel was really lovely. When we arrived, the room was bigger than I expected. The bed is smaller than a normal double in the standard double room. I'm petite and found the bed short. Pay the extra and get a superior room for the bigger bed. We found the Charlesmark really central and the hotel is very close to lots of bars and restaurants. Apart from the size of the bed the hotel really is some thing special. Breakfast was plentiful with a lot of variety.On our final day we left our bags with reception when checking out, So we could do some more sight seeing in this amazing city on our return our bags were just inside the public bar area, there was no bar tender there and our bags could not be seen from reception. We were not happy, we thought they were going to be stored some where safer than very close to the front door. Being completely fair, the reception is very close to front door also and the bar is practically in the reception, they are so close, and I doubt much go's on with out reception knowing. I guess the Bostonians are far more trusting than the Irish. Just to add when I was booking via the internet I found Justin very patient and helpful.Note for management! <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Business Travel Beware (or anyone else seeking comfort or amenities) I was offered this hotel by my corporate travel department -- excited to try a new boutique hotel instead of the standard Marriott, Westin chains, I booked this hotel for a Monday night in Boston. The location is in the heart of Back Bay, but it is definitely not for the business traveler. Beware - there is no parking or valet. You can double park on Boylston Street (arguably one of the busier streets in Boston) and then drive three blocks to the Prudential Parking Lot ($38 for 12 hours). It happened to be raining this day, so I found this particularly uncomfortable. Beware- there is no luggage check or bellperson. The manager offerd to watch my bags while I parked the car. When I returned, I found my bags and briefcase in the middle of the lobby (next to the public bar) and a sign on the front desk that read Manager will return in a moment. I was not pleased that my bags were left unattended in the public lobby, but they were safe and sound, so I just waited for the Manager to reappear. Beware -- the rooms are small. I had a reservation for a king non-smoking room that was reserved with my credit card, including a two day cancellation policy. When I entered my room, I found a tiny full size bed. I returned to the front desk, but was told there were no king size beds available. The manager showed me a list -- apparently I was on the list for King size rooms, but I checked in too late (9pm) and they were all gone. I showed him my confirmed reservation from my corporate travel service (I work for a Fortune 50 company that makes travel arrangements for 30K employees all over the world), but he gazed at me perplexed. I asked him if he could offer me anything else and he said no. I was tired so I returned to my room. I unpacked my suit into a closet the size of a kitchen cabinet (no joke) and put my other clothes in a drawer under the bed.Beware -- there is no place to work. I needed to to check my email and get some work done. I looked around for the desk. I found a writing counter that slid out from under the TV, but didn't know where to sit. I found a folding chair in the kitchen cabinet/closet. The hotel only has wireless internet (the kind you find at the Days Inn type establishments), which wouldn't work with my computer. Frustrated again, I decided to go down to the Lounge and have a drink. Beware -- the lounge/bar closes at 10am. I went down to the lounge at 10:03pm. The bartender abruptly informed me that the lounge was closed. He spun around and continued conversing with his co-worker. Foiled again, I went back to my roomBeware -- the bed is not comforable. I retired to my room and decided to get in bed and watch tv. The bed was hard and the pillows caved into a small ball -- barely providing any support. When even the most basic hotels are upgrading to pillow top mattresses and medium or firm pillows, I was surprised by the lack of comfort. I think this hotel is better suited for Eurpoean leisure travelers on a budget looking for an Ikea-style experience in a good location. Business travelers beware.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Chic  My business colleague and I stayed at the Charlesmark for 2 nights, and both of us loved it! The decor is lovely (Eurochic and very functional -- I love the gray/stainless/red splash look downstairs, and the IKEA look of the rooms), and the location can't be beat! The staff was young and very in-the-know about what was going on in the area, and very efficient. The rooms were small, but no smaller than boutique hotels I've stayed at in London/Notting Hill and Brussells, and both my room and my colleague's (two different single layouts) were very functional; we had no problem working together on a project in the evenings with two laptops and a pile of manuals/spec sheets.The WiFi and in-room entertainment systems were great extras (satellite jazz in the shower is decadent). The rooms offer tiny fridges with bottled water, and the bar downstairs makes a great martini. Didn't stop for continental breakfast, but the spread looked quite nice.I also admit to wandering the halls one night to look at all the artwork... floor 5 has some especially nice around Boston works.I've already passed on business cards for the Charlesmark to 4 friends who travel frequently...

<Author>Book Goddess
<Content>Small, personal and fabulous! This small boutique hotel has great staff and is in perfect location. And I mean GREAT STAFF! Always helpful, quick to respond, personable.The rooms are small but very well appointed with stylish touches such as a huge mirror to create a larger feel to the room. Another touch is the great stereo system in each room. The bathrooms have been upgraded and have glass tile and stone throughout. Very nice shower.Points made in some reviews about plumbing and small rooms with small beds are correct. But the management's response that the small rooms are VERY economical for Boston is well taken, and given that I am a small person, none of this detracted from my stay. My friend had one of the larger rooms and sure enough the bed was larger too.Note that there is no refrigerator in the rooms - but instead a tiny refrigerator/heater that holds a couple of bottles of water. Also, the carpeting in the halls is badly stained. Don't let this keep you from your room, which has fresh paint and is well maintained.I LOVED my stay! The room was quiet, clean and I slept like a log. The buffet breakfast was fine, and the bar at night is great fun. They have a wonderful bartender named Jessica - she rocks.Two big thumbs up, and I would stay again.

<Author>twinklescud
<Content>Excellent Everything My boyfriend and I recently had the pleasure of visiting Boston and staying at the Charlesmark. The hotel is absolutely wonderful (and so fairly priced too)! Our room was very nicely furnished and very modern and the bathroom was very clean with a nice healthy supply of white fluffy towels. The satellite TV was an added bonus. The location is great - very close to the subway station (which can take you practically anywhere in the city and beyond); walking distance to the coolest shops and restaurants and other places like the pharmacy and if need be, the grocery store. My boyfriend and I love to walk so we found it quite convenient to be able to shop downtown and then walk back to the hotel (mind you, it's a bit of a walk but nothing too damaging).The staff was very friendly and helpful. Calvin, in particular, was so fantastic and nice to us that I almost wanted to take him home with me in my luggage. He was so helpful, funny and charming that he made staying at the Charlesmark even better. Thank you, Calvin.With all the great things about this hotel (price, rooms, location, staff) I will definitely stay here again should I have the chance to come back to Boston.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great rates, great service, great bar I spent last weekend at the Charlesmark Hotel and I am thoroughly impressed. With such low rates (under $150) I was a bit suspicious. But my stay was great from the moment I checked in. Calvin at the reception desk went above and beyond, presenting me with a beautiful (and free) map of Boston and informing me where my office was located (I stayed for business). He provided me excellent walking directions, even letting me know where the best restaurants and coffee shops were in that area. That's service.The decor of the hotel and bar is modern, very nice. Everything in the hotel seems brand new. I spent a lot of time at the bar trying their many martini variations. The bartender was friendly, and she put the football game on for me. Best of all she was a bit heavy-handed, which is very necessary in the cold weather.I highly recommend this place to anyone and everyone.

<Author>lisabellab
<Content>Very pleasantly surprised I just returned home from three nights spent at the Charlesmark with my sister and mother. I chose this hotel because of its location, its rates, and the recommendations on this and other Web sites. I was NOT disappointed. We found the staff exceptionally helpful, the rooms very well appointed, and the location highly desirable. If I could improve on anything, it would be the size of our room. (The three of us stayed in a room with one queen bed and a small couch that converted into a bed.)Calvin, Kyle, and Dolores -- the staff members on hand during our stay -- spared nothing to satisfy us. They were friendly, helpful, kind, and accommodating. Our room was tastefully decorated with the latest modern fashions in bedding and accessories. This included a full stereo with CD player, a large television, a cordless phone, cool clock radio, and a miniature (tiny) refrigerator stocked with COMPLIMENTARY bottled water. I almost forgot to mention that they also included a DK Boston guidebook. Even the towels at this place were nice; thick, clean-smelling, new. We all liked the tiled bathroom and the HOT water in the shower.The three of us particularly enjoyed our breakfasts here. We helped ourselves to instant oatmeal, fresh fruit, Dunkin' Donuts goodies, bagels, orange juice, coffee, and hot chocolate. We dined with other hotel guests in the area used nightly as a lounge. It doubled comfortably as breakfast seating while CNN aired on the large-screen television.One of my favorite features of this hotel was the complimentary high-speed Internet access. We were able to check our email, print boarding passes, and take care of any other personal business using the two computers available to guests. Though none of us had laptops with us, we saw others taking advantage of their free wireless Internet access in the lounge.The bar in the lobby of the Charlesmark is something of a spectacle. As a young person, I can say it added to the appeal of the hotel, but I can easily see why my mother wasn't particularly fond of it. Though the bar was quite full at nighttime, we were not at all bothered by its patrons or the din of them enjoying their evenings.I would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone who was travelling to Boston without children. Single people in the 20 - 40 year old range will most certainly enjoy a stay here. The staff truly tried hard to make sure our stay here was enjoyable. I wish I could say that for every hotel!!  
<Date>Nov 14, 2005

<Author>jillhomeuk
<Content>Great hotel...with just a few quirks! We were very impressed with the stylish Charlesmark. We stayed here at the end of our honeymoon, and wanted to finish it in style. The Charlesmark certainly delivered on this score. Previous reviewers may not have got to see the cocktail bar. It is indeed gorgeous, as with everything else here, stylish. The 2 negatives about it though is that while staying here, walking through the entrance to the bar to reach the stairs to our room felt like we were gatecrashing someone elses party. The freely available coffee has also disapeared, but the basic breakfast remains.Our room was in the basement, and didn't smell musty at all, no, not one little bit, instead it smelt a bit like a dentist surgery. Still, once you get used to the rather dark conditions, the rooms are excellent, with some very nice touches. A decent fridge and entertainment system is always very welcome at the end of a long day sightseeing.Location is excellent, the hotel stands on the finish line to the Boston marathon, and is very near the underground railway stop. Despite the proximity of the new bar to our room, we were not disturbed by the noise at all, except for the sound of people coming down the stairs to use the public bathrooms.

<Author>Kazlet
<Content>Good location and good value I've just got back from staying for 5 nights at the Charlesmark. The two best points about the hotel are the location and the fact that it's very clean. The staff are very laid back and friendly; the facilities are good; the breakfast is fine (well it is free); the bed was very comfortable; they have free video loan for guests. I stayed on the third floor in a corner room at the back. I did get a lot of noise during the first night (garbage trucks and deliveries), but otherwise it was fine. Stay here for good value, convenience (4 'T'stops to the Museum of Fine Arts and 4 to Government Centre and the change to the blue line to the Airport), and a friendly welcome. There's a good Thai restaurant next door ('Bangkok Blue'), plus you are just around the block from Newbury Street. Also just opposite is Boston Public Library (try the fab lunch buffet at their restaurant). The only minus point is that to heat the room it appears you have to put the air-con on, which is fairly noisy.

<Author>kejibeard
<Content>Parents Weekend My husband and I have just returned from visiting our daughter at college in Boston for parents weekend. Many of the hotels in the areas surrounding the colleges and universities tend to hike their prices up a bit and many of the 'affordable' hotels are often booked early. In the past we have stayed at the Fairmont Copley, the Hyatt in Cambridge, Marriott and others. The price of the Charlesmark was about $100 less than any of those for this same weekend so we decided to give it a try. So here is my review - the good and the not so good. 1. Location is great. It was raining most of the weekend but it is only about 50 yards to the T stop. The hotel is also an easy walk to just about any type of store or restaurant you could need.2. Hotel Staff: We only met a couple members of the staff the entire time we were there and both were friendly. 3. Our room: Here is where the hotel looses points. From what I've gathered after re-reading all of the prior reviews, we were probably in one of the least desirable rooms of the hotel. Even though we payed extra ($249/ night before taxes) for a 'premium' room, our room was a dark, musty smelling room in the basement with no windows to the outside. The windows that were in the room looked out onto a hallway and have bars on them. Not only does this seem like a fire hazard to me (I asked and this would be a violation in Virginia) but the light from the hallway seeped in thru the shades and made for a miserable nights sleep. On the plus side, the room was very clean.4. Miscellaneous: The hotel makes a big deal about offering 'hundreds of TV channels including movie channels' and bottled water, however out of those hundreds of channels probably less than a dozen actually came in focus. The bottled water is a nice touch but for water drinkers like my husband and myself, 2 small bottles doesn't go very far. Neither was a big deal for us because we are not TV watchers and I didn't mind walking around the corner to the grocery store to buy my own water.Would I stay here again? Not at $249 a night for a basement room. My sister stayed at a bed and breakfast on Beacon Street for about $100 a night the same weekend. No it was not as close to a T stop and no it was not as new  clean feeling but it was a large 4th floor room with real working windows and a refrigerator in the room.If choosing the Charlesmark, ask to not be in a room in the basement and remember, part of what you are paying for is the location. A few blocks further from a T stop will probably save you a hundred dollars a night.  
<Date>Oct 17, 2005

<Author>SommerinTexas
<Content>Would definitely go back! We just got back yesterday from Boston and the Charlesmark Hotel. We stayed there for a 3-night mini-vac and couldn't have been more pleased. The only negative of the place is that the rooms are small. However, they make up for that in every other way. Breakfast is included every morning (pastries, bagels, fruit, coffee, OJ). Your mini fridge is constantly stocked with complimentary bottled water, and if you run out, no problem, they'll immediately get you more. Free computers and internet service are located in the lobby. They also put guide books in every one of their rooms for visitors to use during their stay. It's the little things that count, right? Aside from all these plusses, the location of the hotel couldn't be better. There is a subway stop literally across the street from the hotel, tons of bars and restaurants and shops up and down the street. We highly recommend the Charlesmark, and the next time we go to Boston, we'll definitely stay here again.

<Author>JRO
<Content>Good spot, but a couple of asides - I stayed at the Charlesmark August 26 and 27, and have some mixed feelings. I was generally pleased as it is right in the middle of the Back Bay, literally at the marathon finish line (which may be as close as I ever get to that!) You can walk to most of the sites and activities fairly easily, but know that I walk a lot and this may be daunting for some. It is a 1/2 block from the transit system, though. It is, also, centrally located to tons of restaurants and shopping. The staff ranged from very friendly and accommodating to slighly dazed and spacey - they were all young and not quite professional (but trying). I was left with the impression that everyone trains at some sort of chic hostel. They are in the process of serious renovations or completion of this hotel, so be aware. This isn't necessarily annoying, just a fact. Breakfast is adequate as in muffins, coffee, juice, oatmeal packets, etc. The baked goods were from Dunkin Donuts daily. The rooms are Very small and the bathrooms compact, and I mean small as in you should either be married to or exceptionally good friends with a traveling companion. There was no tub in our bath, but the slate shower was fabulous - good pressure, too. The toilettries are seriously lacking, so pack in. The stereo system is a nice touch - I don't know if this is surround sound or just a small space. Beware that if you are facing Boylston St (as we were) it is quite noisy throughout the wee hours. I'm not convinced my stay was worth quite what I paid for it, but Boston is a pricey town and this is a good location. The rooms and property were very clean.  
<Date>Sep 8, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Boston's charming hotel at great price I avoid huge, impersonal hotels with huge, unconscionable room rates. The Charlesmark is a small boutique hotel off Copley Square in Boston, Mass. We had a wonderful experience over Independence Day weekend. Great view in R. 601, of the park and the historic Boston Library. (Go there: John Adams personal library in Rare Books and a beautiful courtyard). Also see USS Constitution, Old State House, JFK Library, John Adams Historic site in Quincy (subway), walk Beacon Hill, Quincy Market, Freedom Trail. Lots of good restaurants with outdoor seating, and plenty of shops nearby.The staff is very helpful. I had a fractured foot, so they suggested the all-day trolley in lieu of the Freedom Trail. They gave me a surprise treat for my July 4 birthday. They were great with subway directions, and restaurant suggestions. It doesn't stop there. When I left my cell phone charger, they mailed it to me free of charge.One suggestion: To avoid a room mix-up, after you choose and book a room over the phone, ask them to make a notation: Do not move or Keep room-wants view

<Author>CTD5678
<Content>Stylish and small and noisy I stayed for two nights at the Charlesmark and while the experience was okay, there are decided advantages and disadvantages. Location is very convenient to spots downtown and the hotel is clean and service was fine. I really like the sound system and the internet capabilities. The rooms are nicely appointed, but as several other reviewers have noted, quite small. For a single person like myself, that wasn't much of an issue, but I would hesitate to book with another person. Hallways are hard to manage with luggage and certainly if you meet another person! My biggest concern was the noise from floors above and in the hallway at night and the morning, due to the lacki of sound proof.Boston's filled with hotels of quality - this one will has a niche, but will have a hard time competing if its average guest wants to crash after a day around the city.

<Author>slsiege
<Content>Location, Location.... This hotel offers a decent room at a decent price at a great location, a half-block from Copley Square. I could walk almost anywhere I wanted to go: Boston Commons/Public Garden, Quincy Market, Symphony Hall, Fenway Park, and many of the historic sites. (All right, I walk a lot.) Newbury St. is right around the corner. For bad weather or longer hauls, the Copley T stop is steps away. As for the hotel itself, the staff was friendly and usually helpful, the small lounge was nice, and the modest continental breakfast is a plus. So are free local calls and the CD stereo. One odd touch: a tiny refrigerator kept stocked with bottles of spring water. Now for the annoyances. Number one: the rooms are TINY. Mine was just about large enough for myself. Also, there wasn't a closet per se; you have to hang jackets, slacks and shirts in a floor-level cabinet space. (Real wood hangers, though.) Coats go on the hook by the door. Heating/Air Conditioning is on the noisy side, though not egregiously so, but setting the control so that you neither freeze nor roast can be tricky. Operating the cable TV can be a problem for the technologically challenged, and the set is at an odd angle, but you should eventually get the hang of it. My biggest gripe is the lighting: besides the nighttable lamps, there was only a none-too-bright floor lamp. One desk guy told me I could have had another lamp shortly before I was going to check out.Oh, yes, there's a computer and printer in the lounge. But it was virus-ridden and useless when I had to print my return boarding pass. Fortunately there's an internet cafe at 252 Newbury, a couple of blocks away, though it's not open terribly late.The minuses didn't spoil my sleep; that and the location made this a positive experience for me. On my next trip, though, I will check out other hotels as well as this one.

<Author>modoz
<Content>Great location... pity about the rooms The Charlesmark deserves five stars for location and maybe two stars for amenities. The rooms are, in a word, small. I overheard the reception staff describing them as 'European style'. I think they should be more honest. The rooms are really pokey. My husband and I have just returned from a three night stay and I couldn't wait to check out and come home. It was our final desination of a two week holiday in New York and New England and by far the most disappointing accommodation. The bed was small, there was no wardrobe, or anywhere to put our suitcase, and the bathroom was tiny. And this was the second room we were offered! The first room we were allocated was all of the above but had no natural light - the only window looked onto a brick wall. On the plus side, the decor is fresh and modern, and the front desk staff were friendly enough. The location is great - 30 seconds from the T station, which was really handy getting to and from the airport. Breakfast is coffee and bagels, which was nice, but if you want your bagel toasted you have to go two floors down to the basement where you'll find the toaster (annoying). The free internet service didn't work either (very annoying). In summary, I would recommend the Charlesmark for its location and price, but just be aware of what you're getting. It's not a terribly slick operation and I don't think the customer is always put first. Don't go for a standard room, unless you are travelling by yourself. Couples will definitely need more space.

<Author>olderguy47
<Content>Nice place - great location Where to start? I picked this hotel based on reviews on tripadvisor. I was happy with our choice. The location was good for a couple of reasons: a half block from the T, across the street from the Boston Public Library (and a bank of public access computers), and there was a healthy selection of restaurants down Boylston within a few blocks. Also my teenage daughter wanted to go running, and we were three or four blocks from the Charles River with great running paths.There was a mixup when we first got to the hotel. Although we reserved a room to sleep three, it turned out our room was handicap-designated and only slept two. The night clerk made an accomodation for us and we were all happy.The front of the hotel is under construction which really wasn't any problem. The breakfast served in the second floor was quite adequate. We were there three nights. One morning I had a doughnut, the next a blueberry muffin, and the third morning a bagel. The bagels were excellent! Very New York like. Also a bowl of fresh fruit and choice of coffee, tea or OJ. Although breakfast was over at 10 AM, the fruit and remaining goodies were out until evening.My daughter liked that she could play CDs in the full stereo in her room. There is a lending library of VHS movies, but we were always too tired to watch them.There were problems with internet access on the computer in the lounge, but that was okay. There were problems with the soda machine in the basement too (the cans came out hot instead of cold!). But that really didn't overshadow the good value that this hotel was for us. The staff was uniformly helpful and friendly. Restaurants: we liked Legal Seafood at the Pru and the food was really good at The Atlantic Fish Company.We'd gladly come back here again!  
<Date>Apr 9, 2005

<Author>Taffeta
<Content>Fantastic summer stay I stayed at the Charlesmark for about 5 nights or so during July 2004. I loved this hotel. The staff were the best and most helpful of any hotel where I have stayed -- I travel a moderate amount for business purposes.My rate was low, based on my membership in an organization that has negotiated a lower rate with the Charlesmark. I think I had one of their smallest rooms. It was small, but fine for one person. It had what I think was a full-size bed, very comfortable. The room had good lighting, although it took me a little while to figure out how to work the two bedside lights.This hotel had the best audio-video system of any hotel I have ever stayed in. There was a fantastic stereo and sound system -- the TV had satellite rather than cable, and there were far more channels available than most non-digital TV cable systems would have. Also, there were classic videotapes in the lobby that could be brought up to the rooms to watch on the VCR attached to the TV.The only glitch I noticed was that the clothes closet was exceptionally small. It was a waist-high cabinet that was about a foot wide or so. This caused no problems when storing summer clothing... bulky winter clothing would be a different story. Also, it may be that this room had a smaller area for clothing storage than most.When I stayed there, somebody upstairs from me was playing their stereo pretty loudly some of the time. I guess that is a drawback of having such a good stereo system.Overall, I loved this hotel. It is in a great location, and good service is their business!

<Author>marcusg123
<Content>Hidden Gem that Won't be Hidden Much Longer My greatest fear is that everyone writing great reviews for this hotel are going to just lock it out for those of us who want to return. When word fully gets out about this quaint, kitschy, neuvo, funky little place - it will be booked months in advance. The keys here are location and price. You can't beat either. It's not a luxury hotel by any means, but it's comfortable friendly and one of the best situated places I've ever stayed. You just can't be in a better location for the price, which for us was only $149. My wife and I were there the weekend of December 17, 18 and 19 and we shopped til we dropped - literally. This place is in the heart of Copley Square, and close to the T so you don't need a car. We had a blast and the desk support was extremely helpful and friendly. The rooms were cute and dark and fairly small - but frankly - we didn't spend much time there anyway. The room we had faced Boylston Street and was noisy, but we found that if we ran the heat fan in the room, it cut off a lot of the road noise. There's a new lounge going up on the first floor (much needed) but won't be open until spring, I'm told. Just a couple of nitpicky items:- We asked for extra pillows (they are pretty small and flat) and we got two sent to the room without pillowcases- The coffee in the lobby was cold to lukewarm most of the time and not refreshed enough and the doughnuts and bagels from the morning sat there all day and evening. Overall we loved the place and would go back in a second. And will. I just hope the prices don't go up with the demand (hint to ownership).

These special touches one would NOT find at a large, impersonal hotel. The rooms were clean and decorated very tastefully, and all in a fabulous location! We will recommend the Charlesmark to friends, and plan to return again ourselves. Thanks again for a lovely stay.

<Author>AnywhereUSA310
<Content>Not for Business Travel I just returned from a two night business trip to Boston and had a mixed reaction to the Charlesmark.I'll start with the good. I had the larger of the two room sizes and as a solo traveler didn't feel cramped. The room was very clean and, as everyone has noted, tastefully decorated. There was a comfy couch to sit on next to the bed. The bed linens were nice. There were six shelves hung on the wall, which provided a handy place to put travel items and toiletries. The bathroom, though relatively small, was nice with stone floors and nice tile. The lobby had a computer with free internet access - very appreciated by a traveler like me who does not like to cart a laptop in order to be able to check my e-mail. The hotel is very conveniently situated in the Back Bay, near restaurants and shopping. Most restaurants in the neighborhood are open quite late - Gyuhama, a sushi bar down the street, is open until 2:00 a.m. (great for travelers arriving on late flights).Now for the bad. If you are there for business, forget about working in your room at night. There is no desk and no chair. Even worse, even if you want to sit on the comfy couch and go over business papers you can't because the lighting in the room is totally inadequate. (I kept looking for more lights to switch on, but there weren't any). The room does not have a closet. Instead, there is a small cubbyhole under the television which is just tall enough so that you could hang some shirts or blouses, but not long pants, a dress or a long skirt. The only option for those items is the coat rack by the door, which had two hooks. I had a room on Boylston Street and found that the traffic disturbed my sleep (I wish they had double paned the windows to help block out the noise). There were black Venetian blinds instead of blackout shades and curtains -- chic, but the blinds didn't completely block out the street light. Also, don't count on sleeping past 9:00 a.m. - the maids start cleaning the rooms by then and you can hear them outside your room clanging and vacuuming. I wasn't impressed by the free Continental breakfast, especially because there aren't any other real breakfast options in the immediate vicinity. I wished that they had mugs for the coffee and tea rather than crummy paper cups and that they at least had cold cereal in addition to the mediocre bagels and muffins.All in all, if I were traveling to Boston for leisure, wanted a relatively inexpensive place to stay and didn't have a lot of clothes with me that needed to be hung, I would stay at the Charlesmark again. I would not stay there again for a business trip where I needed to work in the room at night.  
<Date>Dec 8, 2004

<Author>SugarWahine
<Content>Can't beat it.... Stayed over Thanksgiving weekend and it was great. <Author>Mozeymo
<Content>Perfect Copley Place Alternative I was in Boston to attend a national conference at the Marriott Copley Place, but thankfully I used expedia and tripadvisor to investigate my options instead dumbly surrendering my wallet to the Marriott just because it was the designated venue for the meeting. The Charlesmark is all of 2 minutes from the front door of the Marriott, and it has infinitely more charm and panache in a smaller package. When my eyes were closed, the smaller room was every bit as expansive as a larger one would have been. The commercial free classical music piped in via the cable system made drifting off to sleep especially easy (the stereo has a sleep timer). I liked the tile work in the bathroom so much I wish I could remodel my bathroom at home to be just like it (the uneven granite on the shower basin feels wonderful on the soles of your feet). This place was great. FYI, try Typhoon (1/2 block the other side of Exeter on Boylston) for tasty pan-Asian dishes (the warm lettuce and chicken appetizer was yummy).
